Evidentiary Rules for Destroyed Mortgaged Property in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling on evidence when the mortgaged property is lost and dispute over its value

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the evidentiary rules for destroyed mortgaged property and apply the principle that the mortgagor's evidence is preferred when claiming higher value.

Core Idea
When the mortgaged property is destroyed, the mortgagor's evidence is accepted for higher value; the mortgagee's denial makes him a guarantor.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the burden of proof when the mortgaged property is lost and the parties dispute its value. Understanding these rules is essential for resolving conflicts in mortgage contracts (rahn) and shows how Hanafi fiqh uses qiyas to analogize from the depositary case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule for destroyed property
Read the first sentence: 'When the property is destroyed, the evidence is for the mortgagor if what he claims is more, because his evidence establishes an increase.' This is the default rule.
The rule applies only when the property is destroyed (halikah).
2
Analyze the qiyas to the depositary case
The text analogizes the mortgagee who denies the mortgage to a depositary who denies a deposit. In Hanafi law, denial of a trust (amanah) transforms the trustee into a guarantor. Here, the mortgagee's denial makes him liable for the full value of the property.
The illa (effective cause) is denial of a trust, which triggers guarantee.
3
Understand the effect of silence
The text states that silence is deemed denial (juhud hukman). Therefore, if the mortgagee remains silent when the property is destroyed, he is treated as if he denied, becoming a guarantor.
This is based on the principle that silence in the face of a claim can be considered admission or denial depending on context.
4
Examine the dispute over the number of items
If the mortgagee claims two garments were pledged and the mortgagor says only one, the mortgagor's statement is taken because the mortgagee is claiming an increase in the mortgage (i.e., more property than agreed). The burden of proof is on the mortgagee.
This follows the general principle that the party claiming an increase bears the burden.
5
Apply the principle of present value witnessing the past
When the property's current value is known (e.g., slave worth 1000 at death) and there is a dispute about its value at the time of pledge, the current value serves as evidence for the past. This is analogous to a mill rental dispute where current water flow indicates past conditions.
The mortgagor's evidence is preferred because it establishes the higher of the two values.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا كانت العين هالكة فالبينة للراهن إذا كان ما يدعيه الراهن أكثر لأن بينته تثبت زيادة. أقام الراهن البينة أنه رهنه عبداً بألف يساوي ألفين وقبضه وأنكر المرتهن يضمن قيمته كلها النصف يسقط بدينه ويؤخذ بالنصف لأنه جحده فصار ضامناً بالجحود كالمودع جحد الوديعة يصير ضامناً للوديعة، وكذلك إن سكت المرتهن ولم يقر ولم يجحد لأن السكوت جحود حكماً ألا ترى لو أخر شيئاً فسكت يسمع عليه كما لو جحد . ولو قال المرتهن تساوي خمسمائة لا يسمع قوله لأنه خلاف ما قامت عليه، ولو قال المرتهن رهنتني هذين الثوبين وقال الراهن أحدهما بعينه فالقول للراهن والبينة للمرتهن لأن المرتهن يدعي عليه زيادة رهن وهو ينكر الرهن. رهن عبداً والدين ألف فذهب عين العبد وهو يساوي ألفاً فقال الراهن كانت هذه قيمته يوم رهنتك فقد ذهب نصف حقك وقال المرتهن بل كانت خمسمائة يومئذ وإزدادت من بعد القول للراهن والبينة له أيضاً لأن القيمة للحال ألف فيكون الحال شاهداً للماضي كمن استأجر طاحونة واختلفا في جريان الماء وانقطاعه يحكم الحال فكذا الراهن بينته تثبت أكثر القيمتين وبينة المرتهن تنفي المثبتة أولى .
And when the property is destroyed, the evidence is for the mortgagor if what he claims is more, because his evidence establishes an increase. The mortgagor brought evidence that he mortgaged a slave worth a thousand for a thousand and took possession, and the mortgagee denied; he guarantees its entire value, half falls due to his debt, and half is taken because he denied, so he becomes a guarantor by denial, like the depositary who denies the deposit becomes a guarantor for the deposit. Similarly, if the mortgagee remained silent and did not affirm or deny, because silence is deemed denial. Do you not see that if someone delayed something and remained silent, it is heard against him as if he denied. And if the mortgagee said it is worth five hundred, his statement is not heard because it contradicts what was established. And if the mortgagee said: You pledged these two garments to me, and the mortgagor said: one of them specifically, then the statement is for the mortgagor and the evidence is for the mortgagee, because the mortgagee claims an increase in mortgage while he denies the mortgage. If he mortgaged a slave and the debt is a thousand, and the slave died while worth a thousand, then the mortgagor said: his value on the day I mortgaged him was this, so half your right is gone, and the mortgagee said: it was five hundred on that day and then increased, the statement is for the mortgagor and the evidence is also for him, because the current value is a thousand, so the present serves as witness for the past, like one who rented a mill and they disputed about the flow and cessation of water; the present situation is judged. So the mortgagor's evidence establishes the higher value and the mortgagee's evidence negates what is established, so the former is more deserving.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage presents rulings for mortgage disputes when the pledged property is destroyed. The key shift: when the property is lost, the mortgagor's evidence is accepted if he claims a higher value, because his evidence establishes an increase (i.e., that the property was worth more, reducing the mortgagee's claim). The author gives an example: if a slave was mortgaged for a thousand and the slave was worth two thousand, and the mortgagee denies, the mortgagee guarantees the full value (two thousand); half (thousand) is offset by the debt, and half is taken from him because his denial made him a guarantor, like a depositary who denies a deposit. Silence also counts as denial. If the mortgagee claims a lower value, his statement is not accepted because it contradicts what was established. Then there is a case where the mortgagee claims two garments were pledged while the mortgagor says only one; the mortgagor's statement is taken because the mortgagee is claiming an increase. Finally, if the slave was worth a thousand at the time of death, and the mortgagor says it was valued at a thousand at pledge, while the mortgagee says it was five hundred and then increased, the mortgagor's statement and evidence prevail because the current value (thousand) witnesses the past, analogous to a mill rental dispute where current flow indicates past condition. The mortgagor's evidence establishes the higher value and is preferred.

Key Terms
هالكة (halikah): Destroyed or lost (the pledged property).
ضامناً بالجحود (daminan bil-juhud): Becoming a guarantor by denying the existence of the contract or property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The mortgagor's, because his evidence establishes an increase.
C) Both equally.
D) Neither; the court decides.

Key Takeaway
When the mortgaged property is destroyed, the mortgagor's evidence is accepted for higher value due to the principle that it establishes an increase; the mortgagee's denial or silence triggers guarantee by analogy to the depositary.

Conflicting Witness Testimony in Mortgage Disputes and Competing Claims
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conflicting testimony and evidence hierarchy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two disciples on conflicting witness testimony in mortgage claims and apply the principle of 'more establishing' evidence (aksar ithbatan) when mortgage competes with other contracts.

Core Idea
When witnesses disagree on the debt amount, Abu Hanifa rejects both testimonies; the two disciples accept the lesser amount.

In mortgage disputes, witness testimony can be conflicting. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on how to handle such conflicts, and the same reasoning extends to competing claims between mortgage and other contracts. This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi dispute and the principles governing evidence preference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed scenario
Read the first part: if the mortgagee denies the mortgage and witnesses disagree on the debt amount (one says 1000, another 2000), what is the ruling according to Abu Hanifa and the two disciples?
Focus on the core issue: disagreement in the subject of testimony.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and dalil
Abu Hanifa rejects both testimonies because the inconsistency prevents establishing the debt, and the mortgage depends on the debt.
His dalil: disagreement in the subject of testimony prevents acceptance.
3
State the two disciples' position and dalil
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad accept the testimony for the lesser amount (1000) if the plaintiff claims the larger, because the mortgage is established for the certain lesser amount.
Their dalil: the witnesses agree on the fact of mortgage, differing only on amount; the lesser is certain.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, the mortgage is invalidated entirely; under the two disciples, it is valid for the lesser amount. The relied-upon view is that of the two disciples.
This practical difference affects the rights of the mortgagee.
5
Apply the reasoning to competing claims
The passage then compares mortgage with deposit, sale, gift, and purchase. Identify the principle: the evidence that establishes a stronger or more binding contract takes precedence (aksar ithbatan).
Mortgage is less binding than sale, so sale evidence prevails; mortgage is more binding than deposit, so mortgage evidence prevails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا أنكر المرتهن الرهن فشهدت إحداهما أنه رهنه بألف والأخرى بألفين لا تقبل لأن الدين بهذه الأشياء لم يثبت عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله لأن اختلاف الشاهدين في المشهود به يمنع قبول الشهادة عنده، وإذا لم يثبت الدين لم يثبت الرهن لأن صحته منوطة بالدين. وعندهما هو رهن بالأقل لأنه يثبت دين ألف بهذه الشهادة عندها إذا كان المدعي يدعي أكثر المالين . ادعى الراهن الرهن بمائة وخمسين وهي قيمته وشهد أحدهما بذلك والآخر بمائة وقال المرتهن عليه مائة وخمسون وهذا رهن بمائة منها فالقول للمرتهن والبينة للراهن لأنه يثبت الدين وهو وخمسون لتصادقهما عليه لا بالبينة وتصادقا أن العين رهن بمائة فصار رهناً بمائة بتصادقهما على ذلك إلا أن بينة الراهن أكثر إثباتاً لأنه يثبت زيادة إيفاء على المرتهن أقام البينة أنه استودعه وهو أقام البينة أنه ارتهنه تقبل بينة المرتهن لأن الرهن جاء لازماً وفيه ضمان ولا لزوم ولا ضمان في الوديعة فكانت بينة الراهن أكثر إثباتاً، ولأنه أمكن العمل بالبينتين بأن يجعل كأنه أودعه ثم رهنه لأن الرهن يرد على الإيداع وأما الإيداع لا يرد على الرهن إلا برضا المرتهن . الراهن أقام البينة على الرهن والآخر على البيع جعل بيعاً لأن البيع لازم من الجانبين وارهن غير لازم من جانب المرتهن والبيع يوجب الملك للحال والرهن لا فكانت بينة البيع أكثر إثباتاً، ولأنه أمكن العمل بالبينتين بأن تجعل كأنه رهن أولاً ثم باع لأن البيع يرد على الرهن والرهن لا يرد على البيع، وكذلك لو ادعى المرتهن الهبة والقبض يؤخذ ببينة الهبة لأن الهبة توجب الملك للحال كالبيع. ادعى الشراء والقبض والآخر ادعى الرهن والقبض يحكم بالشراء إذا كان في يد الراهن، فإن علم بتقدم الرهن جعل رهناً لأن للمرتهن قبضاً معايناً ولا ينقض بالشك كما لو ادعيا الشراء من واحد ولأحدهما قبض معاين وأقاما البينة فصاحب القبض أولى .
And if the mortgagee denies the mortgage, and one witness testified that he mortgaged for a thousand and the other for two thousand, it is not accepted because the debt is not established in the view of Abu Hanifa, because disagreement of witnesses regarding the subject of testimony prevents acceptance of testimony according to him. And if the debt is not established, the mortgage is not established because its validity depends on the debt. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is a mortgage for the lesser amount, because the debt of a thousand is established by this testimony according to them, if the plaintiff claims the larger of the two amounts. The mortgagor claimed the mortgage for one hundred and fifty, which is its value, and one witness testified to that and another to one hundred, and the mortgagee said: he owes one hundred and fifty, and this is a pledge for one hundred of it; the statement is for the mortgagee and the evidence is for the mortgagor, because he establishes the debt of one hundred and fifty by their agreement, not by evidence, and they agree that the property is a pledge for one hundred, so it becomes a pledge for one hundred by their agreement, except that the mortgagor's evidence is more establishing because it proves an increase in payment over the mortgagee. One brought evidence that he deposited it, and the other brought evidence that he took it as mortgage; the mortgagee's evidence is accepted because the mortgage is binding and involves guarantee, while the deposit has no binding or guarantee, so the mortgagee's evidence is more establishing. And because it is possible to act on both evidences by considering it as if he deposited it then mortgaged it, because the mortgage can follow the deposit, whereas the deposit does not follow the mortgage except with the mortgagee's consent. The mortgagor brought evidence of mortgage, and the other (the mortgagee) brought evidence of sale; it is considered a sale because the sale is binding from both sides, while the mortgage is not binding from the mortgagee's side, and the sale gives ownership immediately while the mortgage does not, so the evidence of sale is more establishing. And because it is possible to act on both evidences by considering that he first mortgaged then sold, because the sale can follow the mortgage, while the mortgage cannot follow the sale. Similarly, if the mortgagee claimed a gift and possession, his evidence of gift is taken because the gift gives immediate ownership like sale. If one claimed purchase and possession, and the other claimed mortgage and possession, the purchase is judged if the property is in the mortgagor's hand; if the precedence of mortgage is known, it is considered a mortgage because the mortgagee has an actual possession which cannot be overturned by doubt, just as if two claimed purchase from one person and one has actual possession and both bring evidence, the one with possession is more entitled.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage presents intra-Hanafi dispute on conflicting witness testimony in mortgage claims, and also compares competing claims (mortgage vs. deposit, mortgage vs. sale, etc.). The first issue: if the mortgagee denies the mortgage, and two witnesses disagree on the debt amount (one says 1000, another 2000), Abu Hanifa rejects both testimonies because disagreement prevents establishing the debt; the mortgage fails. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) accept the testimony for the lesser amount (1000) if the plaintiff claims the larger amount, so the mortgage is valid for 1000. Then the author presents several comparisons: when a deposit and mortgage are both claimed with evidence, the mortgagee's evidence prevails because mortgage involves guarantee. When mortgage and sale conflict, sale is given priority because it is binding and transfers ownership immediately. Similarly, gift with possession is like sale. When purchase and mortgage both have evidence and possession, and the property is in the mortgagor's hand, purchase is judged unless the mortgage's precedence is known, in which case the mortgagee's prior possession is respected.

Key Terms
اختلاف الشاهدين (ikhtilaf al-shahidayn): Disagreement between two witnesses regarding the subject of testimony (here, the amount of debt).
الرهن لازم (al-rahn lazim): A binding mortgage; binding on the mortgagor but not initially on the mortgagee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The testimony is rejected entirely.
B) The mortgage is established for the lesser amount.
C) The mortgage is established for the greater amount.
D) The case is dismissed.

Key Takeaway
When witnesses disagree on the debt amount in a mortgage claim, the relied-upon Hanafi position is to accept the testimony for the lesser amount.

Testimony of Mortgage Parties on Third-Party Ownership
Rulings on admissibility of testimony from mortgage parties.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that testimony is rejected when the witness stands to benefit and accepted when the witness stands to harm, using the mortgage scenarios.

Core Idea
Testimony is rejected if the witness derives benefit; accepted if harm is incurred.

This lesson examines three scenarios under mortgage law where the mortgagor or mortgagee testifies that the pledged property actually belongs to a third party. The Hanafi school rules based on whether the witness stands to gain or lose from the testimony. Understanding this principle helps you grasp the broader rule of shubhah (suspicion) in testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties involved
Identify who is testifying: mortgagors (debtors), mortgagees (creditors), or creditors who have a right of retention.
2
Determine the benefit or harm to the witness
For each party, decide whether the testimony, if accepted, would bring them a benefit (gain) or harm (loss).
Benefit makes the testimony rejected; harm makes it accepted.
3
Apply the rule based on benefit
If the testimony benefits the witness, it is rejected due to shubhah (suspicion). If it harms them, it is accepted.
The reasoning: a witness with potential self-interest is not reliable.
4
Consider the status of the pledged property
For mortgagees, distinguish between when the property is still extant vs. destroyed, as this changes benefit/harm.
If the property is destroyed, acceptance of the testimony would benefit the mortgagee (debt extinguished), so testimony is rejected.
5
Analyze the exception: creditors waiving retention
When creditors testify and explicitly say they are satisfied with the debt without the pledge, they are not benefiting, so their testimony is accepted.
This shows that intent matters: they are not trying to revoke the contract, only the security.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو شهد الراهنان بأن المرهون ملك آخر لا تقبل لأنهما بهذه الشهادة يجران لأنفسهما نفعاً ومغنماً لأنهما يريدان إبطال حق المرتهن عن الرهن عليهما، وفي إبطال حق المرتهن عن الرهن نفع لهما في الجملة فتمكنت الشبهة في شهادتهما فلا تقبل ولأن هذه الشهادة في معنى الإقرار لأنهما يشهدان على أنفسهما لأنهما يسعيان في نقض عقد قديم وشهادة الإنسان على نفسه إقرار فهذا إقرار يتضمن إبطال حق المرتهن فلا يصح في حق المرتهن كما لو أقر صريحاً. ولو شهد المرتهنان تقبل لأنهما لا يجران إلى أنفسهما مغنماً ولا يدفعان مغرماً بل يضران بأنفسهما متى كان الرهن قائماً، وإن كان هالكاً لا تقبل شهادتهما لأنهما يمنعان عن أنفسهما مغرماً لأن بهلاك الرهن سقط الدين وبرئ الراهن عن الدين ظاهراً، ومتى قبلت شهادتهما لم يصح الرهن فلا يسقط حقهما. باع رجلان متاعاً بألف درهم من رجل على أن يرهنهما عبداً بعينه ثم شهد أن العبد لرجل وقالا نرضى أن يكون ديناً بالرهن تقبل شهادتهما لأنهما يشهدان على أنفسها بإبطال حقهما في الحبس ولا يجران إلى أنفسهما مغنماً ولا يدفعان مغرماً ولا يسعيان في نقض عقد،
And if the two mortgagors testify that the mortgaged property belongs to another, it is not accepted, because by this testimony they bring benefit and gain to themselves, since they intend to annul the mortgagee's right over the pledge against them, and in annulling the mortgagee's right over the pledge, there is benefit for them in general. Therefore, suspicion attaches to their testimony, so it is not accepted. Also, this testimony is akin to confession because they testify against themselves, as they seek to revoke an old contract. A person's testimony against himself is a confession, and this confession entails annulling the mortgagee's right, so it is not valid with respect to the mortgagee, just as if he explicitly confessed. And if the two mortgagees testify (that the property belongs to another), it is accepted, because they bring no gain to themselves nor ward off harm; rather, they harm themselves when the mortgage is extant. But if the property is destroyed, their testimony is not accepted, because they ward off harm from themselves, since by the destruction of the pledge, the debt falls and the mortgagor is apparently free from the debt. If their testimony were accepted, the mortgage would not be valid, so their right would not fall. Two men sold goods for a thousand dirhams to a man on condition that he pledges a specific slave to them, then he testified that the slave belongs to a man, and they said: we are satisfied that it be a debt with the pledge; their testimony is accepted, because they testify against themselves by annulling their right of retention, and they bring no gain to themselves nor ward off harm, and they do not seek to revoke a contract.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage discusses the admissibility of testimony from the parties in a mortgage regarding the ownership of the pledged property. The first case: two mortgagors (joint debtors) testify that the pledged property belongs to a third party. Their testimony is rejected because they stand to benefit (they want to nullify the mortgagee's right over their property) and because it is essentially a confession against themselves, which cannot affect the mortgagee's rights. The second case: two mortgagees testify that the property belongs to another. If the property is still extant, their testimony is accepted because they are harming themselves (they lose their security). But if the property is destroyed, their testimony is rejected because they would be benefiting themselves (they would avoid losing their debt, since the pledge is already lost). The third case: two creditors (who sold goods on condition of a pledge) testify that the pledged slave belongs to another, but they say they are satisfied to have it as a debt without the pledge. Their testimony is accepted because they are only annulling their right of retention, not gaining anything, and they are not revoking the contract of sale, only the security.

Key Terms
يجران نفعاً (yajjirani naf'an): They bring benefit to themselves; seeking personal advantage.
شبهة (shubhah): Suspicion or ambiguity that impairs testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is the testimony of mortgagees (that the pledged property belongs to another) accepted?
A) Always, because they are neutral.
B) Only when the pledged property is still extant.
C) Only when the pledged property is destroyed.
D) Never, because they are parties to the contract.

Key Takeaway
The admissibility of testimony by mortgage parties hinges on whether the witness gains or loses, not merely on their role in the contract.

Mortgaging an Undivided Share: Inter-Madhhab Dispute and Hanafi Ruling
Explaining the ruling on mortgaging undivided shares with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mortgaging an undivided share, explain the proof based on permanent detention, and distinguish the Shafi'i counter-argument and the intra-Hanafi variation on subsequent common ownership.

Core Idea
Mortgage requires exclusive, continuous detention; an undivided share cannot be detained permanently, so the contract is fasid.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq tackles a key inter-madhhab dispute: Is it valid to mortgage an undivided share (musha') of jointly owned property? The Hanafi school rules it invalid, while the Shafi'i school permits it. Understanding the underlying rationale—whether the purpose of mortgage is detention or sale—is critical for applying the correct ruling. The passage also explores an intra-Hanafi difference on whether later-acquired common ownership voids an existing mortgage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Recognize that the passage addresses the validity of mortgaging an undivided share (musha') in property. Note that the Hanafi position is that it is not permissible, regardless of whether the property is divisible or not.
The term musha' refers to a share that is not physically separated from the whole.
2
State the Hanafi position and its basis
The Hanafi position is that such a mortgage is fasid (defective) if possession is taken (liability attaches), and some say batil (void) which the commentator rejects. The key proof is that mortgage requires permanent detention (habsi da'im), impossible in an undivided share because the pledgee cannot exclusively hold it—partition (muhaya'ah) would disrupt continuous possession.
Possession (qabd) is a condition for completion, not validity, in Hanafi law.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i argument
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that mortgaging a musha' is valid because the purpose of mortgage is sale (bay'), and selling an undivided share is permissible. According to Shafi'is, the mortgage contract aims at eventual sale in case of default, so exclusive physical custody is not essential.
This difference stems from each school's definition of the primary objective (muqtada) of the contract.
4
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafis respond that the primary purpose of mortgage is securing the debt through detention, not sale. Since permanent detention is impossible in a musha', the contract is invalid. They distinguish mortgage from gift and lease: gift only requires transfer of ownership (which can be shared), and lease only requires enabling benefit (which a partner can do).
The distinction hinges on whether the contract requires exclusive physical control.
5
Examine the intra-Hanafi difference on shuyu' tari'
The passage notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to the original narration (riwayat al-asl), if a valid mortgage later becomes subject to common ownership (e.g., through inheritance), the mortgage is invalidated. Abu Yusuf holds it remains valid because continuation is easier than initiation. The commentator prefers the original narration, analogizing to the effect of freedom (hurriyya) in marriage.
This shows that the prevention is due to lack of suitability (mahalliyyah) for detention, which applies equally to initiation and continuation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يجوز ارتهانه والارتهان به وما لا يجوز لما ذكر مقدمات مسائل الرهن ذكر في هذا الباب تفصيل ما يجوز ارتهانه والارتهان به وما لا يجوز إذا لتفصيل إنما يكون بعد الإجمال. قال رحمه الله : ولا يجوز رهن المشاع) يعني لا يصح رهن المشاع فظاهره أنه لا فرق بين ما يحتمل القسمة وما لا يحتمل القسمة. قال صاحب العناية : رهن المشاع قابل القسمة وغيره فاسد يتعلق به الضمان إذا قبض، وقيل باطل لا يتعلق به الضمان وليس بصحيح لأن الباطل منه فيما إذا لم يكن الرهن مالاً ولم يكن المقابل به مضموناً، وما نحن فيه ليس كذلك بناء على أن القبض شرط تمام العقد لا شرط جوازه. وقال الإمام الشافعي رضي الله عنه : يجوز لأن موجبه عنده بيعه والمشاع لا يمتنع بيعه. ولنا أن موجبه ثبوت يد الاستيفاء واستحقاق الحبس الدائم ولا يتصور الحبس الدائم في المشاع لأنه يبطل بالمهايأة قبضه كأنه رهنه يوماً ويوماً ،لا، ولهذا يستوي فيه ما يقبل القسمة وما لا يقبلها بخلاف الهبة حيث تجوز فيما لا يحتمل القسمة لأن موجبها الملك ولا يمتنع بالشيوع، ولا يجوز من شريكه أيضاً لأن ثبوت اليد في المشاع لا يتصور ولأنه لو جاز لأمسكه يوماً بحكم الرهن ويوماً بحكم الملك فيصير كأنه رهنه يوماً ويوماً لا بخلاف الإجارة حيث تجوز في المشاع من الشريك لأن حكمها التمكن من الانتفاع لا الحبس والشريك متمكن من ذلك والشيوع الطارئ يمنع بقاء الرهن في رواية الأصل، وعن أبي يوسف لا يمنع لأن حكم البقاء أسهل من الابتداء فأشبه الهبة وجه الأول أن الامتناع لعدم المحلية وفي مثله يستوي الابتداء والبقاء كالحرية في باب النكاح بخلاف الهبة لأن المشاع لا يمنع وهو الملك والمنع في الابتداء لنفي الغرامة على ما عرف ولا حاجة إلى اعتباره في حالة البقاء، ولهذا يصح الرجوع في بعض الموهوب ولا يصح الفسخ في بعض المرهون . قال في المحيط : ولا يجوز ما هو مشغول بحق الغير ولو رهن عبداً نصفه بستمائة ونصفه بخمسمائة لم يجز لأنه لما النصف بدلاً على حدته صار صفقتين كأنه رهن كل نصف بصفقة في الابتداء فوقع شائعاً فلا يجوز، وهذا يفيد أن المانع هو الإشاعة في العقد لظاهر قوله «فيصير تفريعاً إلى آخره مع أن المانع الإشاعة عند القبض، فلو قال ولا يجوز رهن المشاع عقداً وقبضاً لكان أولى.
Chapter on what is permissible to mortgage and to mortgage with and what is not. When he mentioned the preliminaries of mortgage issues, he mentioned in this chapter the detail of what is permissible to mortgage and to mortgage with and what is not, because detail only comes after summary. He (the author) said: 'And it is not permissible to mortgage an undivided share (musha')' meaning that mortgaging an undivided share is not valid. Its apparent meaning is that there is no difference between what can be divided and what cannot. The author of al-'Inayah said: 'Mortgage of an undivided share, whether divisible or not, is fasid (defective) and entails liability if possession is taken. And it was said it is batil (void) and does not entail liability, but that is not correct because batil applies when the pledged item is not property or the countervalue is not guaranteed, which is not the case here, based on the principle that possession is a condition for completion of the contract, not a condition for its validity.' And Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'It is permissible because its purpose according to him is sale, and an undivided share is not prevented from sale.' And for us (Hanafis), its purpose is the establishment of a right of possession and the right of permanent detention, and permanent detention is inconceivable in an undivided share because it is nullified by partition (muhaya'ah) of possession, as if he mortgaged it one day and one day. Therefore, it is the same whether it can be divided or not, unlike a gift (hibah) which is permissible in what cannot be divided because its purpose is ownership and ownership is not prevented by common ownership. And it is also not permissible from a partner because the establishment of possession in an undivided share is inconceivable, and because if it were permissible, he would hold it one day by virtue of mortgage and one day by virtue of ownership, making it as if he mortgaged it one day and one day. This is unlike a lease (ijarah) which is permissible in an undivided share from a partner because its ruling is enabling benefit, not detention, and the partner is capable of that. And incidental common ownership (al-shuyu' al-tari') prevents the continuation of mortgage according to the original narration, and from Abu Yusuf it does not prevent because the ruling of continuation is easier than initiation, so it resembles a gift. The argument for the first view is that the prevention is due to lack of suitability (mahalliyyah), and in such a case initiation and continuation are the same, like freedom (hurriyyah) in the chapter of marriage, unlike a gift because common ownership does not prevent ownership, and the prevention in initiation is to negate uncertainty (gharamah) as known, and there is no need to consider it in the state of continuation. For this reason, retracting part of a gift is valid, but rescinding part of a mortgage is not valid. He said in al-Muhit: 'And it is not permissible to mortgage what is occupied by the right of another. If a person mortgages a slave, half for six hundred and half for five hundred, it is not valid because when each half is a separate substitute, it becomes two transactions, as if he mortgaged each half in a separate contract initially, thus it becomes common (sha'i') and is not permissible.' And this indicates that the preventing factor is the commonness in the contract, based on the apparent meaning of his statement 'it becomes a branch', etc., even though the preventing factor is commonness at the time of possession. So if he said 'And it is not permissible to mortgage an undivided share in contract and possession', it would be more appropriate.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of mortgaging an undivided share (musha'). The Hanafi position, stated clearly by the author, is that it is not permissible. The commentator elaborates that this applies whether the share is divisible or not. Some scholars (like the author of al-'Inayah) consider such a mortgage fasid (defective) if possession is taken, meaning liability for loss attaches, while others say it is batil (void) with no liability, but the commentator rejects the latter. The key proof for the Hanafis is that mortgage requires permanent detention (habsi da'im), which is impossible in common ownership because the pledgee cannot exclusively hold the property indefinitely—partition (muhaya'ah) would disrupt continuous possession. This is contrasted with sale, where transfer of ownership does not require exclusive physical control, so Shafi'i permits it. The Hanafi argument also compares to gift (hibah), which is valid in undivided shares because ownership can be shared, and lease (ijarah), which is valid from a partner because it only requires enabling benefit, not detention. An intra-Hanafi dispute is noted: according to the original narration (riwayat al-asl), subsequent common ownership (shuyu' tari') after a valid mortgage invalidates it, but Abu Yusuf holds it remains valid because the rules for continuation are easier than initiation. The commentator also discusses a case from al-Muhit where mortgaging two halves of a slave separately with different debts creates common ownership and is invalid, emphasizing that the prohibition is due to commonness at the time of contract, though ideally it should be prohibited both at contract and possession.

Key Terms
مشاع (mushāʿ): An undivided share in a property owned jointly with others, such that the share is not physically separated.
قبض (qabḍ): Possession; taking physical control of the mortgaged item, considered a condition for completion of the mortgage contract (shart tamam al-'aqd) in Hanafi law.
مهايأة (muhāyāʾa): Partition by time or usage among co-owners, dividing the benefit of the shared property.
شيعوع طارئ (shuyūʿ ṭāriʾ): Common ownership that arises after the contract, such as when a mortgaged property becomes shared due to inheritance or mixing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is mortgaging an undivided share invalid?
A) Because an undivided share cannot be sold.
B) Because mortgage requires permanent detention, which is impossible in common ownership.
C) Because possession is not possible in any undivided share.
D) Because the author of al-'Inayah said it is batil.

Key Takeaway
Mortgaging an undivided share is fasid (defective) in Hanafi law because permanent detention is impossible in common ownership.

Mortgaging Disconnected Items and Inclusion of Attachments
Clarifying rulings on mortgaging separate items and what is included in land mortgage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mortgaging detached items and identify which attachments are automatically included in a mortgage of land.

Core Idea
Attached items follow the land in mortgage; detached items cannot be mortgaged alone due to possession impossibility.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq clarifies a key principle in Hanafi mortgage law: the condition of possession (qabḍ) requires that the mortgaged item be physically deliverable. This leads to distinctions between what can be mortgaged independently and what is included as an accessory (tābiʿ). The author first prohibits mortgaging fruit without the tree, crops without land, and trees without land, then explains the underlying rationale and exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited cases
The passage explicitly prohibits mortgaging fruit without the palm tree, crops without the land, and palm trees without the land. Understand these as examples of detached items.
The prohibition applies to anything that is physically attached but sold separately from its base.
2
Understand the legal cause (ʿilla)
Possession (qabḍ) is a condition for mortgage validity. Detached items cannot be possessed independently because they are attached to something else, making them like an undivided share (mushāʿ) where exclusive possession is impossible.
This is a rational proof (dalīl ʿaqlī) by analogy to an undivided share.
3
Note the exception from Abu Hanifa
According to a narration, Abu Hanifa permitted mortgaging land without trees because 'tree' (shajar) refers to plants that can be excluded along with their locations. Contrast this with a house without its building, which is not permitted.
The distinction turns on the meaning of the term 'tree' as a plant that is not considered part of the land's structure.
4
List the inclusions in mortgage of land
When land is mortgaged, all attached items (palm trees, dates on trees, crops, fresh grass, buildings, and plants) are automatically included as tābiʿ (accessories) to validate the contract. This differs from sale, where only palm trees are included by default.
The inclusion is because possession of land necessarily involves possession of attached items.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا الثمرة على النخل دونها ولا زرع في الأرض دونها ولا نخل في الأرض دونها) لأن القبض شرط في الرهن على ما بينا ولا يمكن قبض المتصل وحده فصار في معنى المشاع. وعن أبي حنيفة الله تعالى عنه أن رهن الأرض دون الشجر جائز لأن الشجر اسم للنبات فيكون استثناء الأشجار بمواضعها بخلاف ما إذا رهن الدار دون البناه لأن البناء اسم للمبنى فتكون الأرض جميعاً رهناً وهي مشغولة بملك الراهن، ولو رهن النخل بمواضعها جاز لأنه الأرض بما فيها من النخل وذلك جائز ومجاورة ما ليس برهن لا يمنع الصحة. ويدخل في رهن الأرض النخل والتمر على النخل والزرع والرطبة والبناء والغرس لأنه تابع لاتصاله فيدخل تبعاً تصحيحاً للعقد بخلاف البيع حيث لا تدخل هذه في بيع الأرض سوى النخل لأن الأرض بدون هذه الأشياء جائز فلا حاجة إلى إدخالها في البيع من غير ذكر، وبخلاف المتاع الموضوع بها حيث لا يدخل في الرهن من غير ذكر لأنه ليس بتابع لها ولهذا لو باعها بكل.
He (the author) said: 'And not the fruit on the palm tree without it, nor crops in the land without it, nor palm trees in the land without it' because possession is a condition in mortgage as we have explained, and it is not possible to possess the attached item alone, so it becomes like an undivided share. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa (may Allah be pleased with him) that mortgaging land without trees is permissible because 'tree' (shajar) is a name for plants, so the trees are excluded with their locations, unlike if he mortgages the house without the building (bina') because 'building' is a name for the constructed structure, so the land all becomes mortgaged while it is occupied by the owner's property. And if he mortgages the palm trees with their locations, it is permissible because it is the land including the palm trees, and that is permissible, and adjacency of what is not mortgaged does not prevent validity. And included in the mortgage of land are: palm trees, dates on the palm trees, crops, fresh grass, building, and plants (ghars) because they are attached and thus included as accessories to validate the contract, unlike in sale where these are not included in the sale of land except palm trees, because land without these is permissible (for sale), so there is no need to include them in the sale without mention. And unlike movable goods placed on it, which are not included in the mortgage without mention because they are not attached to it.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the permissibility of mortgaging items that are physically attached to the land but separate in ownership or identification. The author prohibits mortgaging fruit without the tree, crops without land, and trees without land because possession of such items alone is impossible; they are attached to something else, making them analogous to an undivided share where possession is incomplete. Then a narration from Abu Hanifa is reported that mortgaging land without trees is permissible—here 'trees' is interpreted as plants that grow, so the land is mortgaged while the trees are excluded by their locations, similar to how a house cannot be mortgaged without its building because the building is part of the land. However, mortgaging palm trees with their locations (i.e., the land they stand on) is valid because it effectively mortgages the land along with the trees. Finally, the passage explains what is automatically included in the mortgage of land: all attached items such as palm trees, dates, crops, grass, buildings, and plants (ghars). This is because they are considered accessories (tabi') that follow the land to validate the contract. This differs from sale, where only palm trees are included by default; other items are not included because land can be validly sold without them. Movable goods placed on the land are not included because they are not attached.

Key Terms
تابع (tābiʿ): Something that is attached or an accessory to the main object (like trees to land) and thus included in the contract without explicit mention.
قبض (qabḍ): Possession; taking physical control of the mortgaged item. For attached items, possession of the base (land) is necessary.
الزرع (al-zarʿ): Crops growing in the land; included in mortgage of land because they are attached.
الغرس (al-ghars): Plants or seedlings that are planted and attached to the land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is automatically included in the mortgage of land?
A) Only the land itself, nothing else.
B) Attached items like palm trees, crops, and buildings.
C) Movable goods placed on the land.
D) Only palm trees, as in sale.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi mortgage, all items physically attached to the land (tābiʿ) are automatically included to satisfy the possession condition; detached items cannot be mortgaged alone and movable goods are not included.

The Inseparability Rule: Land and Attached Items in Mortgage
Ruling on separating land from trees in mortgage and the reasoning based on possession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on mortgaging land without its attached trees and identify the conditions under which Abu Hanifa permits it.

Core Idea
Attached items automatically enter a mortgage because possession is a condition; land alone cannot be mortgaged without them.

In mortgage, possession is a fundamental condition. The Hanafi school holds that you cannot separate attached items—like trees, crops, or buildings—from the land when mortgaging, because you cannot take possession of them independently. However, Abu Hanifa made a notable exception for trees. This lesson unpacks the rule and its intra-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Find the statement in the text that declares fruit on palms, crops, and palms themselves cannot be mortgaged without the land. Understand that possession (qabd) is the reason.
The text says: 'nor the fruit on the date palms without them, nor crop in the land without it, nor date palms in the land without it'.
2
Understand the rationale
The reason given is that possession is a condition in mortgage, and it is impossible to possess the attached thing alone. It becomes like an undivided share.
Possession of land includes possession of everything attached; without the land, you cannot take control.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's exception
Note that Abu Hanifa held that mortgaging land without trees is permissible because 'tree' is a plant name, and you can except the trees. Compare this with the building case, where the building is a construction that fills the land.
Abu Hanifa's view is a narration; the relied-upon position is the general rule.
4
Apply the distinction
Consider how the ruling differs if the attached item is a building vs. a tree. Buildings are inseparable in concept; trees are separable.
This distinction is based on linguistic and customary interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا الثمرة على النخل دونها ولا زرع في الأرض دونها ولا نخل في الأرض دونها) لأن القبض شرط في الرهن على ما بينا ولا يمكن قبض المتصل وحده فصار في معنى المشاع. وعن أبي حنيفة الله تعالى عنه أن رهن الأرض دون الشجر جائز لأن الشجر اسم للنبات فيكون استثناء الأشجار بمواضعها بخلاف ما إذا رهن الدار دون البناه لأن البناء اسم للمبنى فتكون الأرض جميعاً رهناً وهي مشغولة بملك الراهن، ولو رهن النخل بمواضعها جاز لأنه الأرض بما فيها من النخل وذلك جائز ومجاورة ما ليس برهن لا يمنع الصحة. ويدخل في رهن الأرض النخل والتمر على النخل والزرع والرطبة والبناء والغرس لأنه تابع لاتصاله فيدخل تبعاً تصحيحاً للعقد بخلاف البيع حيث لا تدخل هذه في بيع الأرض سوى النخل لأن الأرض بدون هذه الأشياء جائز فلا حاجة إلى إدخالها في البيع من غير ذكر، وبخلاف المتاع الموضوع بها حيث لا يدخل في الرهن من غير ذكر لأنه ليس بتابع لها ولهذا لو باعها بكل قليل أو كثير هو فيها أو منها لا يدخل المتاع وهذه الأشياء تدخل وكذا تدخل هذه الأشياء في رهن الدار والقرية لما ذكرنا
He (the author) said: (And neither the fruit on the date palms without them, nor crop in the land without it, nor date palms in the land without it) because possession is a condition in mortgage as we have explained, and it is not possible to possess the attached thing alone, so it becomes like an undivided share. From Abu Hanifa: that mortgaging the land without the trees is permissible because 'tree' is a name for the plant, so it is excepting the trees with their places, unlike if he mortgaged the house without the building because 'building' is a name for the constructed thing, so the whole land is mortgaged while it is occupied by the mortgagor's ownership. If he mortgaged the date palms with their places, it is permissible because it is the land with whatever date palms it contains, and that is permissible, and adjacency of what is not mortgaged does not prevent validity. Included in the mortgage of land are: date palms, dates on the palms, crops, fresh grass, buildings, and plantings, because they are attached to it, so they enter as a follow-up to validate the contract, unlike sale where these do not enter into the sale of land except date palms, because the land without these things is permissible, so there is no need to include them in the sale without mention, and unlike goods placed on it, which do not enter into the mortgage without mention because they are not attached to it. For this reason, if he sold it with every little or much that is in it or from it, goods do not enter, but these things do enter. Likewise, these things enter into the mortgage of a house and a village because of what we mentioned.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on mortgaging land without its attached trees, crops, etc. The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that fruit on trees, crops in land, and trees in land cannot be mortgaged separately without the land. The reason is that possession (qabd) is a condition in mortgage, and one cannot take possession of attached items alone—they are inseparable, resembling an undivided share. However, there is a transmission from Abu Hanifa that mortgaging land without trees is permissible because 'tree' refers to a plant that can be excepted, i.e., the trees remain the mortgagor's property. This is different from mortgaging a house without the building (بِناء), because 'building' refers to the constructed structure, and if you except it, the land remains mortgaged while occupied by the building which is the mortgagor's property, causing conflict. Mortgage of trees with their places is allowed because it is essentially the land with trees. Then the passage lists what is automatically included in a mortgage of land: date palms, dates on them, crops, fresh grass, buildings, and plantings. These are attached (muttasil) and thus follow the land to validate the contract. This is unlike sale, where only date palms are included automatically (because they are considered part of the land in sale), but other items like crops and buildings are not included unless mentioned. Goods placed on the land (متاع) are never included without mention because they are not attached. The principle: attached items enter as follow-up (taba'iyyah) to make the mortgage contract valid, since mortgage without possession (which requires physical control) would be invalid. In sale, possession is not an immediate condition, so there is no need to include them automatically.

Key Terms
تابع لاتصاله (tābi' li-ittiṣālihī): A thing that is attached to the main property and thus enters into the mortgage automatically as a follow-up (taba'iyyah) to validate the contract.
متص (muttasil): Physically attached to the land or building, such as trees, crops, buildings; not mere goods placed there.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are fruit on date palms automatically included in a mortgage of land?
A) Because they add value to the mortgage.
B) Because they are attached and cannot be separately possessed.
C) Because the mortgagor's intention is assumed.
D) Because the mortgagee demands it.

Key Takeaway
Attached items (trees, crops, buildings) automatically enter a mortgage of land to satisfy the possession condition, with an intra-Hanafi exception for trees.

Automatic Inclusions in Land Mortgage: The Complete List
List of items automatically included in a land mortgage and the rationale of taba'iyyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the items that automatically enter a mortgage of land and explain the principle of taba'iyyah.

Core Idea
Date palms, crops, grass, buildings, and plantings automatically enter the mortgage because they are attached and needed for possession.

The mortgage of land does not only transfer the soil; it includes everything attached to it that is necessary for valid possession. This lesson examines the specific items listed in the text and the underlying reason: they are included 'as a follow-up' (taba'iyyah) to make the contract valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify each automatically included item
Read the text and list: date palms, dates on palms, crops (زرع), fresh grass (رطبة), buildings (بناء), plantings (غرس).
These are all attached to the land.
2
Understand the condition for automatic inclusion
They must be muttasil (attached). The text says 'because they are attached to it' (لأنه تابع لاتصاله).
Goods (متاع) are not attached, so they are not included.
3
Recognize the purpose: validation of the contract
They enter 'as a follow-up to validate the contract' (تصحيحاً للعقد). Without them, possession would be incomplete.
Mortgage requires full possession; leaving out attached items makes possession impossible.
4
Apply to similar properties
The text says the same rule applies to mortgage of a house (دار) and a village (قرية).
This extends the principle beyond land to any immovable property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا الثمرة على النخل دونها ولا زرع في الأرض دونها ولا نخل في الأرض دونها) لأن القبض شرط في الرهن على ما بينا ولا يمكن قبض المتصل وحده فصار في معنى المشاع. وعن أبي حنيفة الله تعالى عنه أن رهن الأرض دون الشجر جائز لأن الشجر اسم للنبات فيكون استثناء الأشجار بمواضعها بخلاف ما إذا رهن الدار دون البناه لأن البناء اسم للمبنى فتكون الأرض جميعاً رهناً وهي مشغولة بملك الراهن، ولو رهن النخل بمواضعها جاز لأنه الأرض بما فيها من النخل وذلك جائز ومجاورة ما ليس برهن لا يمنع الصحة. ويدخل في رهن الأرض النخل والتمر على النخل والزرع والرطبة والبناء والغرس لأنه تابع لاتصاله فيدخل تبعاً تصحيحاً للعقد بخلاف البيع حيث لا تدخل هذه في بيع الأرض سوى النخل لأن الأرض بدون هذه الأشياء جائز فلا حاجة إلى إدخالها في البيع من غير ذكر، وبخلاف المتاع الموضوع بها حيث لا يدخل في الرهن من غير ذكر لأنه ليس بتابع لها ولهذا لو باعها بكل قليل أو كثير هو فيها أو منها لا يدخل المتاع وهذه الأشياء تدخل وكذا تدخل هذه الأشياء في رهن الدار والقرية لما ذكرنا
He (the author) said: (And neither the fruit on the date palms without them, nor crop in the land without it, nor date palms in the land without it) because possession is a condition in mortgage as we have explained, and it is not possible to possess the attached thing alone, so it becomes like an undivided share. From Abu Hanifa: that mortgaging the land without the trees is permissible because 'tree' is a name for the plant, so it is excepting the trees with their places, unlike if he mortgaged the house without the building because 'building' is a name for the constructed thing, so the whole land is mortgaged while it is occupied by the mortgagor's ownership. If he mortgaged the date palms with their places, it is permissible because it is the land with whatever date palms it contains, and that is permissible, and adjacency of what is not mortgaged does not prevent validity. Included in the mortgage of land are: date palms, dates on the palms, crops, fresh grass, buildings, and plantings, because they are attached to it, so they enter as a follow-up to validate the contract, unlike sale where these do not enter into the sale of land except date palms, because the land without these things is permissible, so there is no need to include them in the sale without mention, and unlike goods placed on it, which do not enter into the mortgage without mention because they are not attached to it. For this reason, if he sold it with every little or much that is in it or from it, goods do not enter, but these things do enter. Likewise, these things enter into the mortgage of a house and a village because of what we mentioned.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on mortgaging land without its attached trees, crops, etc. The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that fruit on trees, crops in land, and trees in land cannot be mortgaged separately without the land. The reason is that possession (qabd) is a condition in mortgage, and one cannot take possession of attached items alone—they are inseparable, resembling an undivided share. However, there is a transmission from Abu Hanifa that mortgaging land without trees is permissible because 'tree' refers to a plant that can be excepted, i.e., the trees remain the mortgagor's property. This is different from mortgaging a house without the building (بِناء), because 'building' refers to the constructed structure, and if you except it, the land remains mortgaged while occupied by the building which is the mortgagor's property, causing conflict. Mortgage of trees with their places is allowed because it is essentially the land with trees. Then the passage lists what is automatically included in a mortgage of land: date palms, dates on them, crops, fresh grass, buildings, and plantings. These are attached (muttasil) and thus follow the land to validate the contract. This is unlike sale, where only date palms are included automatically (because they are considered part of the land in sale), but other items like crops and buildings are not included unless mentioned. Goods placed on the land (متاع) are never included without mention because they are not attached. The principle: attached items enter as follow-up (taba'iyyah) to make the mortgage contract valid, since mortgage without possession (which requires physical control) would be invalid. In sale, possession is not an immediate condition, so there is no need to include them automatically.

Key Terms
تابع لاتصاله (tābi' li-ittiṣālihī): A thing that is attached to the main property and thus enters into the mortgage automatically as a follow-up (taba'iyyah) to validate the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A tent pitched on the land.
B) A building on the land.
C) A pile of firewood on the land.
D) A rented car parked on the land.

Key Takeaway
Attached items (date palms, crops, grass, buildings, plantings) enter a land mortgage automatically to make possession possible; movable goods do not.

Mortgage vs Sale: Why Attached Items Are Treated Differently
Comparison of automatic inclusions in mortgage vs sale and the reasoning based on possession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why attached items like crops and buildings are automatically included in a mortgage but not in a sale (except date palms).

Core Idea
Mortgage requires immediate possession (qabd), so attached items are included automatically; sale does not, so only date palms are included by default.

One of the most interesting contrasts in Hanafi mu'amalat is the difference between mortgage and sale regarding automatically included items. The source passage explicitly compares the two: in mortgage, all attached items enter to satisfy the possession condition; in sale, only date palms are included, and even that is a special case. This lesson explores the reasoning behind this difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mortgage inclusion list
Recall from the previous lesson: date palms, dates, crops, grass, buildings, plantings are automatically included in mortgage.
These are all attached.
2
Identify the sale inclusion list
In sale, the text says only date palms (النخل) are automatically included; crops, grass, buildings, plantings are not.
The reason given: 'because the land without these things is permissible' (جائز).
3
Understand the reason for the difference
Mortgage: possession is a condition, so attached items must be included to make possession valid. Sale: possession is not immediate; the land can be sold empty, and the buyer can later take possession of empty land.
The text says: 'لأن الأرض بدون هذه الأشياء جائز' (land without these things is permissible in sale).
4
Note the exception of date palms in sale
Date palms are included in sale because they are considered part of the land in Hanafi law (they are trees that are a fixture).
This is a special rule for date palms; other trees or plants are not automatically included.
5
Apply the principle to goods (متاع)
Goods are never automatically included in either contract because they are not attached.
The text explicitly states that goods do not enter even if the seller says 'every little or much'.

Source Text

Partial Lawful Recovery in Mortgage
Partial lawful recovery effect on mortgage validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for partial lawful recovery of mortgaged property and determine whether the entire mortgage becomes void or the remainder stands.

Core Idea
Partial recovery voids a mortgage only if the recovered part is undivided or fungible; a specific portion leaves the remainder intact.

When a mortgaged property is partly lawfully recovered (istiḥqāq) because the mortgagor did not own that part, the mortgage does not automatically fail. The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the nature of the recovered portion. This lesson explains that distinction and its practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of recovered part
Determine if the recovered part is a specific, defined portion (muʿayyan) – e.g., a room – or an undivided share (juzʾ shāʾiʿ) or fungible (mithlī) like dates.
The text uses 'موضعاً معيناً' for specific spot, and 'جزءاً شائعاً' or 'ما هو في معنى الشائع كالتمر' for undivided/fungible.
2
Apply the initial mortgageability test
Ask: can the remainder be mortgaged alone initially? If yes, the mortgage continues. If no, the entire mortgage becomes void.
For a specific spot, initial mortgage is permissible; for an undivided share or date, it is not because of uncertainty.
3
Determine the consequence
If the remainder can be mortgaged initially, the mortgage on the remainder is valid. If not, the entire mortgage becomes bāṭil (void).
The rationale: the initial contract is presumed valid; recovery only invalidates if the deficient part taints the whole due to inseparability.
4
Consider the rationale
The rule is based on the nature of the property: a specific portion is separable and can be excluded without affecting the rest, while an undivided share renders the whole uncertain.
This is an application of the principle that validity of part requires the ability to contract on that part alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو استحق بعضه إن كان الباقي يجوز ابتداء الرهن عليه وأخذه جاز وذلك بأن يكون المستحق موضعاً معيناً لأن رهنه ابتداء يجوز فكذا بقاء، وإن كان الباقي لا يجوز ابتداء الرهن عليه بأن استحق جزءاً شائعاً أو ما هو في معنى الشائع كالتمر ونحوه بطل لأنه تبين بالاستحقاق أن الرهن وقع باطلاً ويمنع التسليم كون الراهن أو متاعه في الدار المرهونة حتى إذا رهن داراً وهو فيها وقال سلمتها إليه لا يتم الرهن حتى يقول بعدما خرج من الدار سلمتها إليك لأن التسليم الأول وهو فيها وقع باطلاً لشغلها به، ولا بد من تجديد التسليم بعد الخروج منها كما إذا سلمها ومتاعه فيها ويمنع تسليم الدابة المرهونة الحمل الذي عليها فلا يتم حتى يلقى الحمل بخلاف ما إذا رهن الحمل دونها حتى يكون رهناً إذا دفع الدابة إليه لأن الدار مشغولة فصار كما إذا متاعاً رهن في دار أو في وعاء دون الدار والوعاء بخلاف ما إذا رهن سرجاً على دابة أو الجماماً في رأسها ودفع الدابة مع السرج واللجام حيث لا يكون رهناً حتى ينزعه منها ثم يسلمه إليه لأنه من توابع الدابة بمنزلة الثمرة أحمد للنخل حتى قالوا يدخل في رهن الدابة من غير ذكر
If part of it is lawfully recovered, then if the remainder can be mortgaged initially, taking it is permissible. That is when the lawfully recovered part is a specific spot, because mortgaging it initially is permissible, so likewise as a remainder. If the remainder cannot be mortgaged initially, such as when a undivided part or something resembling undivided like dates and the like is recovered, it becomes void because it becomes clear that the mortgage occurred as void. Delivery is prevented by the presence of the mortgagor or his goods in the mortgaged house. So if he mortgaged a house while he is in it and said, 'I have delivered it to him,' the mortgage is not completed until after he leaves the house and says, 'I have delivered it to you,' because the first delivery while he was in it was void due to it being occupied by him. It is necessary to renew the delivery after leaving it, just as if he delivered it while his goods are in it. Delivery of the mortgaged female animal is prevented by the fetus it carries, so it is not completed until the fetus is delivered, unlike if he mortgaged the fetus without her, such that it becomes a mortgage when he hands over the female animal to him, because the house is occupied, so it becomes like goods mortgaged in a house or a container without the house and the container. Unlike if he mortgaged a saddle on an animal or the rein on its head and delivered the animal with the saddle and rein, where it does not become a mortgage until he removes it from it and then hands it over to him, because it is from the appurtenances of the animal, like fruit on the palm, such that they said: it enters into the mortgage of the animal without mention.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage covers two scenarios: (1) partial lawful recovery (istihqaq) of mortgaged property, and (2) conditions of valid delivery (taslim) when the mortgagor or his belongings occupy the property. First, if part of the mortgaged property is lawfully recovered (e.g., proven to be someone else's), the remaining part is valid only if it is of a type that could be mortgaged alone initially. If the recovered part is a specific, defined portion (e.g., a particular room), the remainder can be mortgaged because it is like a separate property. If the recovered part is an undivided share (juz' sha'i') or something like dates (which are fungible), the entire mortgage becomes void because the initial contract was invalid from the start—the mortgage was not validly constituted. Second, the presence of the mortgagor or his goods in the mortgaged house prevents valid delivery. For a house, if the mortgagor is inside and says 'I have delivered it,' the delivery is void because the house is occupied. He must leave first, then say 'I have delivered it.' Similarly for goods inside. For a female animal, the fetus prevents delivery unless the animal is delivered without the fetus (i.e., the fetus is excluded). If the fetus alone is mortgaged, then delivering the mother counts as delivery of the fetus? Actually the text says: unlike if he mortgaged the fetus alone, then handing over the mother counts as delivery of the fetus? The phrasing is tricky: 'بخلاف ما إذا رهن الحمل دونها حتى يكون رهناً إذا دفع الدابة إليه' meaning if he mortgaged the fetus without the mother, then the delivery of the female animal is valid for the fetus? Actually it says 'حتى يكون رهناً إذا دفع الدابة إليه' (so that it becomes a mortgage when he hands over the female animal to him). The meaning: if the fetus alone is mortgaged, delivery is valid when the mother is delivered, because the fetus is part of her. But if the mother is mortgaged, the fetus must be removed first. Then the rule for saddle and rein: they are appurtenances of the animal, so they automatically enter the mortgage; but if they are on the animal at delivery, they must be removed first? Actually it says: 'بخلاف ما إذا رهن سرجاً على دابة أو الجمام في رأسها ودفع الدابة مع السرج واللجام حيث لا يكون رهناً حتى ينزعه منها ثم يسلمه إليه' meaning if he mortgages a saddle on an animal or the rein on its head, and delivers the animal with the saddle and rein, it is not a mortgage until he removes them and then hands them over. So they are not automatically included in the mortgage of the animal unless mentioned, but if mentioned, they must be physically separated. The text then quotes that they are like fruit on a palm and would enter into the mortgage without mention if they are appurtenances. So there is a nuance: if the animal is mortgaged alone, its appurtenances (saddle, rein) are not automatically included because they are separate property; but if the mortgage is of the animal including its appurtenances, then they must be delivered separately.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istiḥqāq): Lawful recovery of property that was mistakenly included in the mortgage; proves the mortgagor lacked title to that part.
جزء شائع (juzʾ shāʾiʿ): An undivided share in a property that is not physically separated, e.g., half of a house without demarcation.
موضع معين (mawḍiʿ muʿayyan): A specific, defined portion of a property, e.g., a room, identifiable by boundaries.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mortgaged house is partly lawfully recovered (istihqaq) and the recovered part is a specific, defined room, what happens to the mortgage of the remaining part?
A) The entire mortgage becomes void.
B) The remaining part remains valid as a mortgage because it can be mortgaged initially.
C) The mortgage becomes void only if the recovered part is more than half.
D) The mortgagee must return the remaining part to the mortgagor.

Key Takeaway
Partial lawful recovery voids a mortgage only when the recovered portion is undivided or fungible; a specific separable portion leaves the remainder valid.

Delivery Conditions When Mortgagor Occupies Property
Conditions and obstacles for valid delivery in mortgage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the obstacles preventing valid delivery of mortgaged property and state the remedies required by Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Delivery of mortgaged property is invalid if the mortgagor or his goods occupy it; vacating and re-delivering with explicit statement are required.

Valid delivery (taslīm) of mortgaged property is essential for the mortgage to be complete. The Hanafi school rules that delivery must be actual and unimpeded. This lesson covers the obstacles to delivery—such as the presence of the mortgagor, his goods, or a fetus—and the necessary steps to achieve valid delivery.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obstacle
Check whether the mortgagor himself, his goods, or an attached item (e.g., fetus, saddle) occupies the property at the time of delivery.
The text gives examples: 'كون الراهن أو متاعه في الدار' and 'الحمل الذي عليها'.
2
Effect on delivery
Initial delivery while the obstacle exists is void (bāṭil) because the property is not fully yielded.
The text says 'وقع باطلاً لشغلها به' – it was void due to occupancy.
3
Determine the remedy
The obstacle must be removed: the mortgagor must vacate, goods removed, fetus delivered or animal freed, etc. Then a new delivery must be performed with explicit words.
For a house: depart then say 'I have delivered it.' For a fetus: deliver it first, then the mother.
4
Distinguish special cases
For appurtenances like saddle/rein on an animal, they may need separate removal and delivery unless they are explicitly included in the mortgage. For a fetus mortgaged alone, delivery of the mother suffices.
The contrast is made with 'بخلاف' (unlike) clauses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو استحق بعضه إن كان الباقي يجوز ابتداء الرهن عليه وأخذه جاز وذلك بأن يكون المستحق موضعاً معيناً لأن رهنه ابتداء يجوز فكذا بقاء، وإن كان الباقي لا يجوز ابتداء الرهن عليه بأن استحق جزءاً شائعاً أو ما هو في معنى الشائع كالتمر ونحوه بطل لأنه تبين بالاستحقاق أن الرهن وقع باطلاً ويمنع التسليم كون الراهن أو متاعه في الدار المرهونة حتى إذا رهن داراً وهو فيها وقال سلمتها إليه لا يتم الرهن حتى يقول بعدما خرج من الدار سلمتها إليك لأن التسليم الأول وهو فيها وقع باطلاً لشغلها به، ولا بد من تجديد التسليم بعد الخروج منها كما إذا سلمها ومتاعه فيها ويمنع تسليم الدابة المرهونة الحمل الذي عليها فلا يتم حتى يلقى الحمل بخلاف ما إذا رهن الحمل دونها حتى يكون رهناً إذا دفع الدابة إليه لأن الدار مشغولة فصار كما إذا متاعاً رهن في دار أو في وعاء دون الدار والوعاء بخلاف ما إذا رهن سرجاً على دابة أو الجماماً في رأسها ودفع الدابة مع السرج واللجام حيث لا يكون رهناً حتى ينزعه منها ثم يسلمه إليه لأنه من توابع الدابة بمنزلة الثمرة أحمد للنخل حتى قالوا يدخل في رهن الدابة من غير ذكر
If part of it is lawfully recovered, then if the remainder can be mortgaged initially, taking it is permissible. That is when the lawfully recovered part is a specific spot, because mortgaging it initially is permissible, so likewise as a remainder. If the remainder cannot be mortgaged initially, such as when a undivided part or something resembling undivided like dates and the like is recovered, it becomes void because it becomes clear that the mortgage occurred as void. Delivery is prevented by the presence of the mortgagor or his goods in the mortgaged house. So if he mortgaged a house while he is in it and said, 'I have delivered it to him,' the mortgage is not completed until after he leaves the house and says, 'I have delivered it to you,' because the first delivery while he was in it was void due to it being occupied by him. It is necessary to renew the delivery after leaving it, just as if he delivered it while his goods are in it. Delivery of the mortgaged female animal is prevented by the fetus it carries, so it is not completed until the fetus is delivered, unlike if he mortgaged the fetus without her, such that it becomes a mortgage when he hands over the female animal to him, because the house is occupied, so it becomes like goods mortgaged in a house or a container without the house and the container. Unlike if he mortgaged a saddle on an animal or the rein on its head and delivered the animal with the saddle and rein, where it does not become a mortgage until he removes it from it and then hands it over to him, because it is from the appurtenances of the animal, like fruit on the palm, such that they said: it enters into the mortgage of the animal without mention.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage covers two scenarios: (1) partial lawful recovery (istihqaq) of mortgaged property, and (2) conditions of valid delivery (taslim) when the mortgagor or his belongings occupy the property. First, if part of the mortgaged property is lawfully recovered (e.g., proven to be someone else's), the remaining part is valid only if it is of a type that could be mortgaged alone initially. If the recovered part is a specific, defined portion (e.g., a particular room), the remainder can be mortgaged because it is like a separate property. If the recovered part is an undivided share (juz' sha'i') or something like dates (which are fungible), the entire mortgage becomes void because the initial contract was invalid from the start—the mortgage was not validly constituted. Second, the presence of the mortgagor or his goods in the mortgaged house prevents valid delivery. For a house, if the mortgagor is inside and says 'I have delivered it,' the delivery is void because the house is occupied. He must leave first, then say 'I have delivered it.' Similarly for goods inside. For a female animal, the fetus prevents delivery unless the animal is delivered without the fetus (i.e., the fetus is excluded). If the fetus alone is mortgaged, then delivering the mother counts as delivery of the fetus? Actually the text says: unlike if he mortgaged the fetus alone, then handing over the mother counts as delivery of the fetus? The phrasing is tricky: 'بخلاف ما إذا رهن الحمل دونها حتى يكون رهناً إذا دفع الدابة إليه' meaning if he mortgaged the fetus without the mother, then the delivery of the female animal is valid for the fetus? Actually it says 'حتى يكون رهناً إذا دفع الدابة إليه' (so that it becomes a mortgage when he hands over the female animal to him). The meaning: if the fetus alone is mortgaged, delivery is valid when the mother is delivered, because the fetus is part of her. But if the mother is mortgaged, the fetus must be removed first. Then the rule for saddle and rein: they are appurtenances of the animal, so they automatically enter the mortgage; but if they are on the animal at delivery, they must be removed first? Actually it says: 'بخلاف ما إذا رهن سرجاً على دابة أو الجمام في رأسها ودفع الدابة مع السرج واللجام حيث لا يكون رهناً حتى ينزعه منها ثم يسلمه إليه' meaning if he mortgages a saddle on an animal or the rein on its head, and delivers the animal with the saddle and rein, it is not a mortgage until he removes them and then hands them over. So they are not automatically included in the mortgage of the animal unless mentioned, but if mentioned, they must be physically separated. The text then quotes that they are like fruit on a palm and would enter into the mortgage without mention if they are appurtenances. So there is a nuance: if the animal is mortgaged alone, its appurtenances (saddle, rein) are not automatically included because they are separate property; but if the mortgage is of the animal including its appurtenances, then they must be delivered separately.

Key Terms
تسليم (taslīm): Delivery of the mortgaged property to the mortgagee; necessary for completion of the contract.
شغل (shughl): Occupancy or preoccupation of the property by the mortgagor or his belongings, which prevents valid delivery.
الحمل (al-ḥaml): Fetus of an animal; its presence in the mother prevents valid delivery of the mother as a mortgage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required to make delivery of a mortgaged house valid when the mortgagor is inside at the time of the initial delivery statement?
A) The mortgagee must enter the house.
B) The mortgagor must leave the house and then re-declare delivery.
C) The initial statement suffices despite the presence.
D) The house must be re-mortgaged after vacating.

Key Takeaway
Valid delivery of mortgaged property requires that the property be free of the mortgagor and his goods; any occupancy invalidates delivery, and a fresh explicit delivery is needed after vacating.
