Wife's Suretyship and Selling the Pledge
Fatwa on sale of pledge when surety imprisoned.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling the pledge when a surety is imprisoned and identify the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa denies selling the pledge when a third-party surety is imprisoned; Sahibayn allow it.

This passage presents a case where a wife becomes surety for her husband's debt with his permission. When the judge imprisons her for inability to pay, the question arises: can the pledge be sold to discharge the debt? The response reveals a disagreement between the founding Hanafi imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their roles
The pledger (husband), mortgagee (creditor), and surety (wife who becomes kafil). Note that the wife's surety is with her husband's permission.
Kafalah requires consent.
2
State the problem
The surety is imprisoned for inability to pay. The mortgagee demands the pledge be sold.
3
Extract the two positions
According to Abu Hanifa (Imam): no sale. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): yes, sale is allowed.
The text says 'على قول الإمام،لا، وعلى قولهما نعم'.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, the mortgagee cannot force sale; under Sahibayn, the judge may sell the pledge.
This ikhtilaf is within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرهن باب ما يجوز ارتهانه والارتهان به وما لا يجوز
بسبب
هذه
yضمن. وكذا ذكر ذلك الحلواني في شرحه وسئل الخجندي عن رجل رهن عند آخر وكفلت زوجته لرب الدين بإذن الزوج فطالب رب الدين الكفيل بإيفاء الذين فحبسه القاضي أن وعجز عن أدائه هل للقاضي يبيع الرهن ؟ قال : على قول الإمام،لا، وعلى قولهما نعم . وسئل أبو الفضل عن رجل رهن عند آخر داراً إلى سنة بدين على الراهن وقبض الدار هل يكون التأجيل مفسداً للرهن؟ قال : إن كان الأجل في الرهن فسد، وإن كان في الدين لا يفسد. وهكذا في الإيضاح سئل عن المرتهن إذا مات وورثته يعرفون بالرهن ولا يعرفون الراهن ويطلبون الخروج عن العهدة هل يكون حكمه حكم اللقطة؟ قال : يحفظ حتى يظهر المالك. وفي التجريد لو رهن عبدين أو ثوبين ولم يسم لكل واحد شيئاً . من الدين يقسم الدين على قيمة تلك الأشياء، فما أصاب كل واحد وهو مضمون بأقل من قيمته ومما سمى أو رهن شاتين بثلاثين أحدهما بعشرة والأخرى بعشرين ولم يبين أيهما لم يجز لأن الجهالة تقع بينهما منازعة عند الهلاك فإنه إذا هلكت إحداهما لا يدري لا يسقط من الدين بأداء عشرة أو عشرين فيتنازعان في ذهاب الدين ،بهلاكها، فلو بين فهلك إحداهما سقط من الدين بقدرها لأنه لما بين حصة كل واحد منهما من الدين انقطعت المنازعة. وفي المنتقى : ولو قال رهنتك النخل بأصوله جاز إذا سمى بأصوله وإن لم يسم بأصوله لم يجز لأنه لا يقوم إلا بأصوله فلا يمكن تسليمه ،بدونه وذكر الفقيه أبو الليث روى أبو يوسف عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى في رجل رهن عند رجل جارية لها زوج فالرهن جائز لأن النكاح لا يوجب نقصاً في الرق والمالية وليس للمرتهن منع الزوج من غشيانها لأنه رهنها وهي مشغولة بحق الزوج وحق المرتهن لا يتعلق بمنافع البضع فحق الزوج فيها لا يفسد الرهن، فإن وطئها من ذلك سقط الدين لأن الوطء من الزوج ليس بجناية فأشبه الموت من المرض. قال أبو يوسف رحمه الله تعالى : ولو رهن جارية لا زوج لها فزوجها الراهن برضى المرتهن فهذا مثل الأول، ولو زوجها بغير رضا المرتهن جاز النكاح لقيام ملكه فيها وللمرتهن أن يمنعه من غشيانها لأن النكاح لم يعقد برضاه وثبوت حقه من الحبس سابق على تعلق حق الزوج غشيها فالمهر رهن معها، وإن لم يغشها لم يكن المهر رهناً معها لأن له أن يمنعه من الوطء فإن مات من غشيانها، فإن شاء المرتهن ضمن الراهن وإن شاء ضمن الزوج، فإن ضمن الزوج يرجع على المولى إن كتم الرهن عنه لأنه هو الذي أوقعه فيه، وإن لم يكن كتمه عنه لا يرجع . ابن سماعة عن أي يوسف رحمه الله : رجل أعتق ما في بطن جاريته ثم رهنها المولى فالرهن جائز لأنها مملوكة لمولاه، وإن ولدت فنقصتها الولادة لم يذهب من الدين شيء بنقصان الولادة لأنه إذا رهنها وهي حامل والحمل لا له من الولادة والولادة لا تنفك عن النقصان عادة فهذا النقصان حصل بسبب في يد الراهن فلا يكون مضموناً على المرتهن، ولو كان عليه دينار فدفع إليه دينارين فقال خذ أحدهما قضاء يكون لك فضاعا قبل أن أخذ فدينه
Book of Pledge: Chapter on what is permissible to take as pledge and what to pledge with and what is not permissible. Because of this, it is guaranteed. And likewise al-Halwani mentioned in his commentary. And al-Khujandi was asked about a man who pledged with another and his wife became surety for the debt owner with the husband's permission, then the debt owner demanded the surety to pay off the debt, so the judge imprisoned him and he was unable to pay; does the judge have the right to sell the pledge? He said: according to the Imam's statement, no; according to them both, yes. And Abu al-Fadl was asked about a man who pledged a house with another for one year for a debt on the pledger and the mortgagee took possession of the house; does the term invalidate the pledge? He said: if the term was in the pledge, it is invalid; if it was in the debt, it is not invalid. Likewise in al-Idah, he was asked about the mortgagee if he dies and his heirs know of the pledge but do not know the pledger and they seek to be free of responsibility; is its ruling the ruling of a lost item? He said: it is kept until the owner appears. In al-Tajrid: if he pledges two slaves or two garments and does not specify anything of the debt for each, the debt is divided according to the value of those items; what befalls each is guaranteed by the lesser of its value and what was specified. Or if he pledges two sheep for thirty, one for ten and the other for twenty, and he does not specify which, it is not valid because uncertainty leads to dispute upon destruction; for if one perishes, it is not known whether ten or twenty is discharged from the debt, so they dispute. If he specifies, and one perishes, that amount is discharged from the debt because when he specified the share of each from the debt, dispute is cut off. In al-Muntaqa: if he says 'I pledge the palm trees with their roots to you', it is valid if he specifies 'with their roots'; if he does not specify, it is not valid because they are only valuable with their roots, so delivery is not possible without them. And al-Faqih Abu al-Layth mentioned: Abu Yusuf reported from Abu Hanifa regarding a man who pledges a slave-girl who has a husband; the pledge is valid because marriage does not cause diminishment in slavery and value, and the mortgagee cannot prevent the husband from having intercourse with her because he pledged her while she is occupied with the husband's right, and the mortgagee's right does not attach to the usufruct of the vulva, so the husband's right does not invalidate the pledge. If he dies from that intercourse, the debt is discharged because the husband's intercourse is not a crime, so it resembles death from illness. Abu Yusuf said: if he pledges a slave-girl without a husband and the pledger marries her with the mortgagee's consent, this is like the first case. If he marries her without the mortgagee's consent, the marriage is valid due to his ownership, and the mortgagee can prevent him from intercourse because the marriage was not contracted with his consent and his right of detention preceded the husband's right. If he has intercourse with her, the dowry is pledged with her; if he does not have intercourse, the dowry is not pledged with her because he can prevent intercourse. If she dies from his intercourse, the mortgagee may either hold the pledger liable or hold the husband liable. If he holds the husband liable, the husband may recourse to the master if he concealed the pledge from him; if he did not conceal it, he cannot recourse. Ibn Sama'ah from Abu Yusuf: a man emancipated what was in the belly of his slave-girl, then the master pledged her; the pledge is valid because she is owned by her master. If she gives birth and the delivery diminishes her, nothing of the debt is lost due to the diminishment because when he pledged her while she was pregnant and delivery necessarily causes diminishment, this diminishment occurred by a cause in the pledger's hand, so it is not guaranteed upon the mortgagee. If he owed a dinar and gave him two dinars and said 'take one as payment and it is for you,' and they perished before he took, his debt is [unfinished].
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on various issues related to the validity and effects of pledges (rahn). It opens with a case involving a wife's suretyship: if she becomes a surety with her husband's permission and the judge imprisons her due to inability to pay, can the pledge be sold? Abu Hanifa says no, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say yes. Next, a term (ajal) in the pledge itself invalidates it, but a term in the debt does not. If the mortgagee dies and heirs know of the pledge but not the pledger, the pledge is treated like a lost item until the owner appears. When multiple items are pledged without specifying each's portion of the debt, the debt is divided proportionally to value; if one perishes, only its portion is discharged. If two sheep are pledged for thirty, one for ten and the other for twenty, specifying is necessary to avoid disputes. Pledging palm trees with roots is valid if specified; without specification it is invalid because roots are essential. A married slave-girl can be pledged because marriage does not reduce her value; the mortgagee cannot prevent the husband's intercourse. If the husband's intercourse causes her death, the debt is discharged. If the pledger marries a slave-girl after pledging her without the mortgagee's consent, the mortgagee can prevent intercourse. If she dies from intercourse, the mortgagee may choose whom to hold liable. A pregnant slave-girl can be pledged; if delivery diminishes her value, no compensation is required. The last case about two dinars is incomplete but shows the importance of specifying the purpose (payment vs pledge) when giving money.

Key Terms
الرهن (al-rahn): A property given as security for a debt, which the creditor holds but may not use without permission.
الكفالة (al-kafalah): Suretyship; a guarantee to fulfill an obligation. Here, the wife becomes surety for the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Khujandi's fatwa, when a wife becomes surety with husband's permission and is imprisoned for inability to pay, what is Abu Hanifa's ruling on selling the pledge?
A) The pledge may be sold.
B) The pledge may not be sold.
C) The pledge must be sold.
D) The pledge is forfeited.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of selling a pledge when a surety defaults is disputed within the Hanafi school; Abu Hanifa prohibits, Sahibayn allow.

Term in Pledge vs. Term in Debt
Fatwa on effect of term on pledge validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a term inserted in the pledge contract (invalid) and a term in the underlying debt (valid), and state the ruling.

Core Idea
A term in the pledge invalidates the contract; a term in the debt does not.

This passage answers whether adding a time limit to a pledge contract affects its validity. Abu al-Fadl clarifies that if the term is within the pledge itself (e.g., pledge for one year), the contract is invalid. However, if the term refers to the repayment of the debt (e.g., debt due in one year), the pledge remains valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Scenario 1: The term is part of the pledge contract (e.g., 'I pledge this house for one year'). Scenario 2: The term is part of the debt agreement (e.g., 'I owe you this money for one year').
2
Extract the ruling for each
For scenario 1: the pledge is invalid (فسد). For scenario 2: the pledge is not invalid (لا يفسد).
The text says 'إن كان الأجل في الرهن فسد، وإن كان في الدين لا يفسد'.
3
Understand the rationale
Pledge is a contract of immediate security; adding a term contradicts its nature. The debt's term is separate and does not affect the pledge's validity.
Hanafi fiqh emphasizes that rahn is a contract of trust and immediate possession.

Source Text

وهكذا في الإيضاح سئل عن المرتهن إذا مات وورثته يعرفون بالرهن ولا يعرفون الراهن ويطلبون الخروج عن العهدة هل يكون حكمه حكم اللقطة؟ قال : يحفظ حتى يظهر المالك. وفي التجريد لو رهن عبدين أو ثوبين ولم يسم لكل واحد شيئاً . من الدين يقسم الدين على قيمة تلك الأشياء، فما أصاب كل واحد وهو مضمون بأقل من قيمته ومما سمى أو رهن شاتين بثلاثين أحدهما بعشرة والأخرى بعشرين ولم يبين أيهما لم يجز لأن الجهالة تقع الدين انقطعت المنازعة. وفي المنتقى : ولو قال رهنتك النخل بأصوله جاز إذا سمى بأصوله وإن لم يسم بأصوله لم يجز لأنه لا يقوم إلا بأصوله فلا يمكن تسليمه ،بدونه وذكر الفقيه أبو الليث روى أبو يوسف عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى في رجل رهن عند رجل جارية لها زوج فالرهن جائز لأن النكاح لا يوجب نقصاً في الرق والمالية وليس للمرتهن منع الزوج من غشيانها لأنه رهنها وهي مشغولة بحق الزوج وحق المرتهن لا يتعلق بمنافع البضع فحق الزوج فيها لا يفسد الرهن، فإن وطئها من ذلك سقط الدين لأن الوطء من الزوج ليس بجناية فأشبه الموت من المرض. قال أبو يوسف رحمه الله تعالى : ولو رهن جارية لا زوج لها فزوجها الراهن برضى المرتهن فهذا مثل الأول، ولو زوجها بغير رضا المرتهن جاز النكاح لقيام ملكه فيها وللمرتهن أن يمنعه من غشيانها لأن النكاح لم يعقد برضاه وثبوت حقه من الحبس سابق على تعلق حق الزوج غشيها فالمهر رهن معها، وإن لم يغشها لم يكن المهر رهناً معها لأن له أن يمنعه من الوطء فإن مات من غشيانها، فإن شاء المرتهن ضمن الراهن وإن شاء ضمن الزوج، فإن ضمن الزوج يرجع على المولى إن كتم الرهن عنه لأنه هو الذي أوقعه فيه، وإن لم يكن كتمه عنه لا يرجع . ابن سماعة عن أي يوسف رحمه الله : رجل أعتق ما في بطن جاريته ثم رهنها المولى فالرهن جائز لأنها مملوكة لمولاه، وإن ولدت فنقصتها الولادة لم يذهب من الدين شيء بنقصان الولادة لأنه إذا رهنها وهي حامل والحمل لا له من الولادة والولادة لا تنفك عن النقصان عادة فهذا النقصان حصل بسبب في يد الراهن فلا يكون مضموناً على المرتهن، ولو كان عليه دينار فدفع إليه دينارين فقال خذ أحدهما قضاء يكون لك فضاعا قبل أن أخذ فدينه
Book of Pledge: Chapter on what is permissible to take as pledge and what to pledge with and what is not permissible. Because of this, it is guaranteed. And likewise al-Halwani mentioned in his commentary. And al-Khujandi was asked about a man who pledged with another and his wife became surety for the debt owner with the husband's permission, then the debt owner demanded the surety to pay off the debt, so the judge imprisoned him and he was unable to pay; does the judge have the right to sell the pledge? He said: according to the Imam's statement, no; according to them both, yes. And Abu al-Fadl was asked about a man who pledged a house with another for one year for a debt on the pledger and the mortgagee took possession of the house; does the term invalidate the pledge? He said: if the term was in the pledge, it is invalid; if it was in the debt, it is not invalid. Likewise in al-Idah, he was asked about the mortgagee if he dies and his heirs know of the pledge but do not know the pledger and they seek to be free of responsibility; is its ruling the ruling of a lost item? He said: it is kept until the owner appears. In al-Tajrid: if he pledges two slaves or two garments and does not specify anything of the debt for each, the debt is divided according to the value of those items; what befalls each is guaranteed by the lesser of its value and what was specified. Or if he pledges two sheep for thirty, one for ten and the other for twenty, and he does not specify which, it is not valid because uncertainty leads to dispute upon destruction; for if one perishes, it is not known whether ten or twenty is discharged from the debt, so they dispute. If he specifies, and one perishes, that amount is discharged from the debt because when he specified the share of each from the debt, dispute is cut off. In al-Muntaqa: if he says 'I pledge the palm trees with their roots to you', it is valid if he specifies 'with their roots'; if he does not specify, it is not valid because they are only valuable with their roots, so delivery is not possible without them. And al-Faqih Abu al-Layth mentioned: Abu Yusuf reported from Abu Hanifa regarding a man who pledges a slave-girl who has a husband; the pledge is valid because marriage does not cause diminishment in slavery and value, and the mortgagee cannot prevent the husband from having intercourse with her because he pledged her while she is occupied with the husband's right, and the mortgagee's right does not attach to the usufruct of the vulva, so the husband's right does not invalidate the pledge. If he dies from that intercourse, the debt is discharged because the husband's intercourse is not a crime, so it resembles death from illness. Abu Yusuf said: if he pledges a slave-girl without a husband and the pledger marries her with the mortgagee's consent, this is like the first case. If he marries her without the mortgagee's consent, the marriage is valid due to his ownership, and the mortgagee can prevent him from intercourse because the marriage was not contracted with his consent and his right of detention preceded the husband's right. If he has intercourse with her, the dowry is pledged with her; if he does not have intercourse, the dowry is not pledged with her because he can prevent intercourse. If she dies from his intercourse, the mortgagee may either hold the pledger liable or hold the husband liable. If he holds the husband liable, the husband may recourse to the master if he concealed the pledge from him; if he did not conceal it, he cannot recourse. Ibn Sama'ah from Abu Yusuf: a man emancipated what was in the belly of his slave-girl, then the master pledged her; the pledge is valid because she is owned by her master. If she gives birth and the delivery diminishes her, nothing of the debt is lost due to the diminishment because when he pledged her while she was pregnant and delivery necessarily causes diminishment, this diminishment occurred by a cause in the pledger's hand, so it is not guaranteed upon the mortgagee. If he owed a dinar and gave him two dinars and said 'take one as payment and it is for you,' and they perished before he took, his debt is [unfinished].
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on various issues related to the validity and effects of pledges (rahn). It opens with a case involving a wife's suretyship: if she becomes a surety with her husband's permission and the judge imprisons her due to inability to pay, can the pledge be sold? Abu Hanifa says no, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say yes. Next, a term (ajal) in the pledge itself invalidates it, but a term in the debt does not. If the mortgagee dies and heirs know of the pledge but not the pledger, the pledge is treated like a lost item until the owner appears. When multiple items are pledged without specifying each's portion of the debt, the debt is divided proportionally to value; if one perishes, only its portion is discharged. If two sheep are pledged for thirty, one for ten and the other for twenty, specifying is necessary to avoid disputes. Pledging palm trees with roots is valid if specified; without specification it is invalid because roots are essential. A married slave-girl can be pledged because marriage does not reduce her value; the mortgagee cannot prevent the husband's intercourse. If the husband's intercourse causes her death, the debt is discharged. If the pledger marries a slave-girl after pledging her without the mortgagee's consent, the mortgagee can prevent intercourse. If she dies from intercourse, the mortgagee may choose whom to hold liable. A pregnant slave-girl can be pledged; if delivery diminishes her value, no compensation is required. The last case about two dinars is incomplete but shows the importance of specifying the purpose (payment vs pledge) when giving money.

Key Terms
الرهن (al-rahn): A property given as security for a debt, which the creditor holds but may not use without permission.
الأجل (al-ajal): A term or deferment of payment or possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a man says to the creditor, 'I pledge this house to you for one year'?
A) The pledge is valid.
B) The pledge is invalid.
C) The pledge is valid only if the debt is also for one year.
D) The pledge is valid but the term is void.

Key Takeaway
A term inserted into the pledge contract invalidates it, but a term in the debt does not affect the pledge's validity.

Rahn — Pledge
beginner
4 min
Mortgagee Dies, Pledger Unknown – Pledge as Luqata
Fatwa on handling pledge when pledger unknown.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that when the mortgagee dies and the heirs do not know the pledger, the pledge is treated like a found object (luqata) until the owner appears.

Core Idea
An unidentified pledge is preserved as a trust until the pledger is found, like a lost item.

This passage deals with a situation where the mortgagee dies and his heirs know of the pledge but cannot identify the pledger. They seek to be relieved of responsibility. The ruling is clear: the pledge is kept like a found object (luqata) until the pledger appears. It is not forfeited or sold.

Guided Path
1
Identify the situation
The mortgagee dies; his heirs know there is a pledge but do not know the pledger (debtor). They ask how to handle it.
2
Apply the analogy to luqata
The pledge is similar to a lost item (luqata) because the owner is unknown. The heirs must preserve it and make efforts to find the owner.
The text says 'حكمه حكم اللقطة' (its ruling is the ruling of luqata).
3
State the ruling
The pledge is kept (يحفظ) until the owner (the pledger) appears.
The heirs cannot dispose of it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرهن باب ما يجوز ارتهانه والارتهان به وما لا يجوز
بسبب
هذه
yضمن. وكذا ذكر ذلك الحلواني في شرحه وسئل الخجندي عن رجل رهن عند آخر وكفلت زوجته لرب الدين بإذن الزوج فطالب رب الدين الكفيل بإيفاء الذين فحبسه القاضي أن وعجز عن أدائه هل للقاضي يبيع الرهن ؟ قال : على قول الإمام،لا، وعلى قولهما نعم . وسئل أبو الفضل عن رجل رهن عند آخر داراً إلى سنة بدين على الراهن وقبض الدار هل يكون التأجيل مفسداً للرهن؟ قال : إن كان الأجل في الرهن فسد، وإن كان في الدين لا يفسد. وهكذا في الإيضاح سئل عن المرتهن إذا مات وورثته يعرفون بالرهن ولا يعرفون الراهن ويطلبون الخروج عن العهدة هل يكون حكمه حكم اللقطة؟ قال : يحفظ حتى يظهر المالك. وفي التجريد لو رهن عبدين أو ثوبين ولم يسم لكل واحد شيئاً . من الدين يقسم الدين على قيمة تلك الأشياء، فما أصاب كل واحد وهو مضمون بأقل من قيمته ومما سمى أو رهن شاتين بثلاثين أحدهما بعشرة والأخرى بعشرين ولم يبين أيهما لم يجز لأن الجهالة تقع بينهما منازعة عند الهلاك فإنه إذا هلكت إحداهما لا يدري لا يسقط من الدين بأداء عشرة أو عشرين فيتنازعان في ذهاب الدين ،بهلاكها، فلو بين فهلك إحداهما سقط من الدين بقدرها لأنه لما بين حصة كل واحد منهما من الدين انقطعت المنازعة. وفي المنتقى : ولو قال رهنتك النخل بأصوله جاز إذا سمى بأصوله وإن لم يسم بأصوله لم يجز لأنه لا يقوم إلا بأصوله فلا يمكن تسليمه ،بدونه وذكر الفقيه أبو الليث روى أبو يوسف عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى في رجل رهن عند رجل جارية لها زوج فالرهن جائز لأن النكاح لا يوجب نقصاً في الرق والمالية وليس للمرتهن منع الزوج من غشيانها لأنه رهنها وهي مشغولة بحق الزوج وحق المرتهن لا يتعلق بمنافع البضع فحق الزوج فيها لا يفسد الرهن، فإن وطئها من ذلك سقط الدين لأن الوطء من الزوج ليس بجناية فأشبه الموت من المرض. قال أبو يوسف رحمه الله تعالى : ولو رهن جارية لا زوج لها فزوجها الراهن برضى المرتهن فهذا مثل الأول، ولو زوجها بغير رضا المرتهن جاز النكاح لقيام ملكه فيها وللمرتهن أن يمنعه من غشيانها لأن النكاح لم يعقد برضاه وثبوت حقه من الحبس سابق على تعلق حق الزوج غشيها فالمهر رهن معها، وإن When the mortgagee dies and the pledger is unknown, what is the ruling?
A) The pledge is divided among the heirs.

Rahn — Pledge
intermediate

Multiple Items Pledged without Allocation of Debt
Fatwa on allocating debt among multiple pledged items.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that when multiple items are pledged without specifying each item's share of the debt, the debt is divided proportionally to value, and failing to specify shares leads to invalidity if it causes uncertainty.

Core Idea
Uncertainty in apportionment of debt among multiple pledged items invalidates the pledge if it leads to disputes.

This passage addresses two scenarios: (1) two slaves or garments pledged without specifying each one's portion of the debt – the debt is divided according to value. (2) Two sheep pledged for specific amounts (e.g., one for ten, one for twenty) without identifying which sheep is for which – the pledge is invalid because the uncertainty leads to disputes upon destruction. The key is that jahalah (uncertainty) that can cause dispute invalidates the contract.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two scenarios
Scenario A: Multiple homogeneous items (e.g., two slaves) with no specification of each's debt share. Scenario B: Multiple items with individual prices but no assignment (e.g., one sheep for 10, one for 20, but not saying which is which).
2
Rule for Scenario A
The debt is divided proportionally to the value of the items. Each item's value is determined, and the debt is allocated accordingly.
The text says 'يقسم الدين على قيمة تلك الأشياء'.
3
Rule for Scenario B
If each item has a specific price but no specification of which item corresponds to which price, the pledge is invalid due to uncertainty that leads to dispute upon destruction.
The text says 'لم يجز لأن الجهالة تقع بينهما منازعة عند الهلاك'.
4
Condition for validity
The pledger must specify precisely which item covers which portion of the debt. If he does, and one item perishes, that portion is discharged without dispute.

Source Text

Book of Pledge: Chapter on what is permissible to take as pledge and what to pledge with and what is not permissible. Because of this, it is guaranteed. And likewise al-Halwani mentioned in his commentary. And al-Khujandi was asked about a man who pledged with another and his wife became surety for the debt owner with the husband's permission, then the debt owner demanded the surety to pay off the debt, so the judge imprisoned him and he was unable to pay; does the judge have the right to sell the pledge? He said: according to the Imam's statement, no; according to them both, yes. And Abu al-Fadl was asked about a man who pledged a house with another for one year for a debt on the pledger and the mortgagee took possession of the house; does the term invalidate the pledge? He said: if the term was in the pledge, it is invalid; if it was in the debt, it is not invalid. Likewise in al-Idah, he was asked about the mortgagee if he dies and his heirs know of the pledge but do not know the pledger and they seek to be free of responsibility; is its ruling the ruling of a lost item? He said: it is kept until the owner appears. In al-Tajrid: if he pledges two slaves or two garments and does not specify anything of the debt for each, the debt is divided according to the value of those items; what befalls each is guaranteed by the lesser of its value and what was specified. Or if he pledges two sheep for thirty, one for ten and the other for twenty, and he does not specify which, it is not valid because uncertainty leads to dispute upon destruction; for if one perishes, it is not known whether ten or twenty is discharged from the debt, so they dispute. If he specifies, and one perishes, that amount is discharged from the debt because when he specified the share of each from the debt, dispute is cut off. In al-Muntaqa: if he says 'I pledge the palm trees with their roots to you', it is valid if he specifies 'with their roots'; if he does not specify, it is not valid because they are only valuable with their roots, so delivery is not possible without them. And al-Faqih Abu al-Layth mentioned: Abu Yusuf reported from Abu Hanifa regarding a man who pledges a slave-girl who has a husband; the pledge is valid because marriage does not cause diminishment in slavery and value, and the mortgagee cannot prevent the husband from having intercourse with her because he pledged her while she is occupied with the husband's right, and the mortgagee's right does not attach to the usufruct of the vulva, so the husband's right does not invalidate the pledge. If he dies from that intercourse, the debt is discharged because the husband's intercourse is not a crime, so it resembles death from illness. Abu Yusuf said: if he pledges a slave-girl without a husband and the pledger marries her with the mortgagee's consent, this is like the first case. If he marries her without the mortgagee's consent, the marriage is valid due to his ownership, and the mortgagee can prevent him from intercourse because the marriage was not contracted with his consent and his right of detention preceded the husband's right. If he has intercourse with her, the dowry is pledged with her; if he does not have intercourse, the dowry is not pledged with her because he can prevent intercourse. If she dies from his intercourse, the mortgagee may either hold the pledger liable or hold the husband liable. If he holds the husband liable, the husband may recourse to the master if he concealed the pledge from him; if he did not conceal it, he cannot recourse. Ibn Sama'ah from Abu Yusuf: a man emancipated what was in the belly of his slave-girl, then the master pledged her; the pledge is valid because she is owned by her master. If she gives birth and the delivery diminishes her, nothing of the debt is lost due to the diminishment because when he pledged her while she was pregnant and delivery necessarily causes diminishment, this diminishment occurred by a cause in the pledger's hand, so it is not guaranteed upon the mortgagee. If he owed a dinar and gave him two dinars and said 'take one as payment and it is for you,' and they perished before he took, his debt is [unfinished].
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on various issues related to the validity and effects of pledges (rahn). It opens with a case involving a wife's suretyship: if she becomes a surety with her husband's permission and the judge imprisons her due to inability to pay, can the pledge be sold? Abu Hanifa says no, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say yes. Next, a term (ajal) in the pledge itself invalidates it, but a term in the debt does not. If the mortgagee dies and heirs know of the pledge but not the pledger, the pledge is treated like a lost item until the owner appears. When multiple items are pledged without specifying each's portion of the debt, the debt is divided proportionally to value; if one perishes, only its portion is discharged. If two sheep are pledged for thirty, one for ten and the other for twenty, specifying is necessary to avoid disputes. Pledging palm trees with roots is valid if specified; without specification it is invalid because roots are essential. A married slave-girl can be pledged because marriage does not reduce her value; the mortgagee cannot prevent the husband's intercourse. If the husband's intercourse causes her death, the debt is discharged. If the pledger marries a slave-girl after pledging her without the mortgagee's consent, the mortgagee can prevent intercourse. If she dies from intercourse, the mortgagee may choose whom to hold liable. A pregnant slave-girl can be pledged; if delivery diminishes her value, no compensation is required. The last case about two dinars is incomplete but shows the importance of specifying the purpose (payment vs pledge) when giving money.

Key Terms
الجهالة (al-jahalah): Uncertainty or ambiguity in a contract that leads to disputes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling when a man pledges two sheep, one for ten and one for twenty, without specifying which is which?
A) Valid, proportional division applies.
B) Valid, the mortgagee decides.
C) Invalid, because of uncertainty leading to dispute.
D) Invalid, because sheep cannot be pledged individually.

Key Takeaway
When multiple items are pledged with specific debt amounts, precise identification of each item is required; otherwise uncertainty invalidates the pledge.

Pledging Palm Trees with or without Roots
Fatwa on pledge of palm trees with or without roots.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that pledging palm trees is valid only if they are specified 'with roots', because without roots they cannot be delivered.

Core Idea
Delivery of the pledge is essential; if the roots are not included, the trees cannot be surrendered, making the contract invalid.

This passage addresses the pledge of palm trees. The key issue is that palm trees are valuable only when accompanied by their roots, as roots are necessary for their survival and possession. Therefore, if the pledge does not explicitly include the roots ('بأصوله'), the contract is invalid because the pledge cannot be effectively delivered to the mortgagee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The passage asks about pledging palm trees with or without specifying 'with roots'.
2
Extract the ruling
If the pledger says 'I pledge the palm trees with their roots', it is valid. If he does not specify 'with roots', it is invalid.
The text says 'جاز إذا سمى بأصوله وإن لم يسم بأصوله لم يجز'.
3
Understand the rationale
The trees are only valuable and can only be delivered (for the mortgagee to possess) if the roots are included. Without roots, the trees cannot be removed from the ground effectively, so delivery is impossible.
The text says 'لأنه لا يقوم إلا بأصوله فلا يمكن تسليمه بدونه'.

Source Text

yضمن. وكذا ذكر ذلك الحلواني في شرحه وسئل الخجندي عن رجل رهن عند آخر وكفلت زوجته لرب الدين بإذن الزوج فطالب رب الدين الكفيل بإيفاء الذين فحبسه القاضي أن وعجز عن أدائه هل للقاضي يبيع الرهن ؟ قال : على قول الإمام،لا، وعلى قولهما نعم . وسئل أبو الفضل عن رجل رهن عند آخر داراً إلى سنة بدين على الراهن وقبض الدار هل يكون التأجيل مفسداً للرهن؟ قال : إن كان الأجل في الرهن فسد، وإن كان في الدين لا يفسد. وهكذا في الإيضاح سئل عن المرتهن إذا مات وورثته يعرفون بالرهن ولا يعرفون الراهن ويطلبون الخروج عن العهدة هل يكون حكمه حكم اللقطة؟ قال : يحفظ حتى يظهر المالك. وفي التجريد لو رهن عبدين أو ثوبين ولم يسم لكل واحد شيئاً . من الدين يقسم الدين على قيمة تلك الأشياء، فما أصاب كل واحد وهو مضمون بأقل من قيمته ومما سمى أو رهن شاتين بثلاثين أحدهما بعشرة والأخرى بعشرين ولم يبين أيهما لم يجز لأن الجهالة تقع بينهما منازعة عند الهلاك فإنه إذا هلكت إحداهما لا يدري لا يسقط من الدين بأداء عشرة أو عشرين فيتنازعان في ذهاب الدين ،بهلاكها، فلو بين فهلك إحداهما سقط من الدين بقدرها لأنه لما بين حصة كل واحد منهما من الدين انقطعت المنازعة. وفي المنتقى : ولو قال رهنتك النخل بأصوله جاز إذا سمى بأصوله وإن لم يسم بأصوله لم يجز لأنه لا يقوم إلا بأصوله فلا يمكن تسليمه ،بدونه وذكر الفقيه أبو الليث روى أبو يوسف عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى في رجل رهن عند رجل جارية لها زوج فالرهن جائز لأن النكاح لا يوجب نقصاً في الرق والمالية وليس للمرتهن منع الزوج من غشيانها لأنه رهنها وهي مشغولة بحق الزوج وحق المرتهن لا يتعلق بمنافع البضع فحق الزوج فيها لا يفسد الرهن، فإن وطئها من ذلك سقط الدين لأن الوطء من الزوج ليس بجناية فأشبه الموت من المرض. قال أبو يوسف رحمه الله تعالى : ولو رهن جارية لا زوج لها فزوجها الراهن برضى المرتهن فهذا مثل الأول، ولو زوجها بغير رضا المرتهن جاز النكاح لقيام ملكه فيها وللمرتهن أن يمنعه من غشيانها لأن النكاح لم يعقد برضاه وثبوت حقه من الحبس سابق على تعلق حق الزوج غشيها فالمهر رهن معها، وإن لم يغشها لم يكن المهر رهناً معها لأن له أن يمنعه من الوطء فإن مات من غشيانها، فإن شاء المرتهن ضمن الراهن وإن شاء ضمن الزوج، فإن ضمن الزوج يرجع على المولى إن كتم الرهن عنه لأنه هو الذي أوقعه فيه، وإن لم يكن كتمه عنه لا يرجع . ابن سماعة عن أي يوسف رحمه الله : رجل أعتق ما في بطن جاريته ثم رهنها المولى فالرهن جائز لأنها مملوكة لمولاه، وإن ولدت فنقصتها الولادة لم يذهب من الدين شيء بنقصان الولادة لأنه إذا رهنها وهي حامل والحمل لا له من الولادة والولادة لا تنفك عن النقصان عادة فهذا النقصان حصل بسبب في يد الراهن فلا يكون مضموناً على المرتهن، ولو كان عليه دينار فدفع إليه دينارين فقال خذ أحدهما قضاء يكون لك فضاعا قبل أن أخذ فدينه

Married Slave-girl as Pledge – Husband's Intercourse and Death
Fatwa on pledging a married slave-girl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain that a married slave-girl can be pledged, the mortgagee cannot prevent the husband's intercourse, and if she dies from intercourse, the debt is discharged.

Core Idea
Marriage does not reduce a slave-girl's value; the husband's marital rights do not invalidate the pledge, and death from marital intercourse discharges the debt.

This passage from Abu Yusuf's report of Abu Hanifa addresses the pledge of a slave-girl who has a husband. It clarifies that her marriage does not diminish her value or prevent the validity of the pledge. The mortgagee cannot interfere with the husband's conjugal rights. Importantly, if the husband's intercourse causes her death, it is not treated as a crime but as an act of the husband, and the debt is discharged because the pledged property is lost without fault of the mortgagee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
The case is a slave-girl (jariyah) who is already married. She is pledged to a creditor.
2
Extract the ruling on validity
The pledge is valid because marriage does not cause deficiency in her value (مالية).
The text says 'فالرهن جائز لأن النكاح لا يوجب نقصاً في الرق والمالية'.
3
State the mortgagee's limitation
The mortgagee cannot prevent the husband from having intercourse because the marital right predates the pledge and does not diminish the property's value.
The text says 'ليس للمرتهن منع الزوج من غشيانها'.
4
Ruling upon death from intercourse
If the husband's intercourse causes her death, the debt is discharged (يسقط الدين). This is because the husband's act is not a crime (جناية) but a lawful act, and the loss is attributed to the pledger's side.
The text says 'فإن وطئها من ذلك سقط الدين لأن الوطء من الزوج ليس بجناية فأشبه الموت من المرض'.

Or if he pledges two sheep for thirty, one for ten and the other for twenty, and he does not specify which, it is not valid because uncertainty leads to dispute upon destruction; for if one perishes, it is not known whether ten or twenty is discharged from the debt, so they dispute. If he specifies, and one perishes, that amount is discharged from the debt because when he specified the share of each from the debt, dispute is cut off. In al-Muntaqa: if he says 'I pledge the palm trees with their roots to you', it is valid if he specifies 'with their roots'; if he does not specify, it is not valid because they are only valuable with their roots, so delivery is not possible without them. And al-Faqih Abu al-Layth mentioned: Abu Yusuf reported from Abu Hanifa regarding a man who pledges a slave-girl who has a husband; the pledge is valid because marriage does not cause diminishment in slavery and value, and the mortgagee cannot prevent the husband from having intercourse with her because he pledged her while she is occupied with the husband's right, and the mortgagee's right does not attach to the usufruct of the vulva, so the husband's right does not invalidate the pledge. If he dies from that intercourse, the debt is discharged because the husband's intercourse is not a crime, so it resembles death from illness. Abu Yusuf said: if he pledges a slave-girl without a husband and the pledger marries her with the mortgagee's consent, this is like the first case. If he marries her without the mortgagee's consent, the marriage is valid due to his ownership, and the mortgagee can prevent him from intercourse because the marriage was not contracted with his consent and his right of detention preceded the husband's right. If he has intercourse with her, the dowry is pledged with her; if he does not have intercourse, the dowry is not pledged with her because he can prevent intercourse. If she dies from his intercourse, the mortgagee may either hold the pledger liable or hold the husband liable. If he holds the husband liable, the husband may recourse to the master if he concealed the pledge from him; if he did not conceal it, he cannot recourse. Ibn Sama'ah from Abu Yusuf: a man emancipated what was in the belly of his slave-girl, then the master pledged her; the pledge is valid because she is owned by her master. If she gives birth and the delivery diminishes her, nothing of the debt is lost due to the diminishment because when he pledged her while she was pregnant and delivery necessarily causes diminishment, this diminishment occurred by a cause in the pledger's hand, so it is not guaranteed upon the mortgagee. If he owed a dinar and gave him two dinars and said 'take one as payment and it is for you,' and they perished before he took, his debt is [unfinished].
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on various issues related to the validity and effects of pledges (rahn). It opens with a case involving a wife's suretyship: if she becomes a surety with her husband's permission and the judge imprisons her due to inability to pay, can the pledge be sold? Abu Hanifa says no, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say yes. Next, a term (ajal) in the pledge itself invalidates it, but a term in the debt does not. If the mortgagee dies and heirs know of the pledge but not the pledger, the pledge is treated like a lost item until the owner appears. When multiple items are pledged without specifying each's portion of the debt, the debt is divided proportionally to value; if one perishes, only its portion is discharged. If two sheep are pledged for thirty, one for ten and the other for twenty, specifying is necessary to avoid disputes. Pledging palm trees with roots is valid if specified; without specification it is invalid because roots are essential. A married slave-girl can be pledged because marriage does not reduce her value; the mortgagee cannot prevent the husband's intercourse. If the husband's intercourse causes her death, the debt is discharged. If the pledger marries a slave-girl after pledging her without the mortgagee's consent, the mortgagee can prevent intercourse. If she dies from intercourse, the mortgagee may choose whom to hold liable. A pregnant slave-girl can be pledged; if delivery diminishes her value, no compensation is required. The last case about two dinars is incomplete but shows the importance of specifying the purpose (payment vs pledge) when giving money.

Key Terms
البضع (al-bud'): The vulva or sexual usufruct; the right to sexual enjoyment within marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a married slave-girl pledged as security dies from her husband's intercourse, what happens to the debt?
A) The debt remains, and the mortgagee can claim from the husband.
B) The debt is discharged.
C) The debt is halved.
D) The mortgagee can sell the pledge.

Key Takeaway
A married slave-girl can be pledged, and the mortgagee cannot interfere with marital rights; death from marital intercourse cancels the debt.

Pledging a Slave-girl then Marrying Her – with and without Mortgagee's Consent
Fatwa on marrying a pledged slave-girl after pledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between marrying a pledged slave-girl with and without the mortgagee's consent, stating the consequences for dowry and liability upon death.

Core Idea
Marriage after pledge without mortgagee's consent allows the mortgagee to prevent intercourse; with consent, the mortgagee cannot. Liability for death differs accordingly.

This passage, attributed to Abu Yusuf, expands on the previous case. If a slave-girl is pledged and then the pledger marries her to someone (or to himself) with the mortgagee's consent, the ruling is similar to the case of a pre-existing marriage. However, if the marriage is without consent, the mortgagee can prevent intercourse. The dowry (mahr) becomes part of the pledge only if intercourse occurs. If she dies from intercourse, the mortgagee has the option to hold either the pledger or the husband liable.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish two scenarios
Scenario A: The pledger marries the slave-girl with the mortgagee's consent. Scenario B: He marries her without consent.
2
Ruling for Scenario A (with consent)
The mortgagee cannot prevent intercourse. If intercourse occurs, the dowry (mahr) is also pledged. If she dies from intercourse, the debt is discharged (as before).
The text says 'فهذا مثل الأول' (this is like the first case).
3
Ruling for Scenario B (without consent)
The marriage is valid because the pledger still owns her. However, the mortgagee can prevent the husband from intercourse because the mortgagee's right of detention (حق الحبس) predates the husband's right.
The text says 'وللمرتهن أن يمنعه من غشيانها لأن النكاح لم يعقد برضاه وثبوت حقه من الحبس سابق'.
4
Effect on dowry and liability
If the husband does have intercourse (despite mortgagee's prevention), the dowry becomes pledged with her. If she dies from intercourse, the mortgagee may choose whom to hold liable: the pledger or the husband. If he holds the husband liable, the husband can recourse to the pledger if the pledger concealed the pledge; otherwise no recourse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرهن باب ما يجوز ارتهانه والارتهان به وما لا يجوز
بسبب
هذه
yضمن. وكذا ذكر ذلك الحلواني في شرحه وسئل الخجندي عن رجل رهن عند آخر وكفلت زوجته لرب الدين بإذن الزوج فطالب رب الدين الكفيل بإيفاء الذين فحبسه القاضي أن وعجز عن أدائه هل للقاضي يبيع الرهن ؟ قال : على قول الإمام،لا، وعلى قولهما نعم . وسئل أبو الفضل عن رجل رهن عند آخر داراً إلى سنة بدين على الراهن وقبض الدار هل يكون التأجيل مفسداً للرهن؟ قال : إن كان الأجل في الرهن فسد، وإن كان في الدين لا يفسد. وهكذا في الإيضاح سئل عن المرتهن إذا مات وورثته يعرفون بالرهن ولا يعرفون الراهن ويطلبون الخروج عن العهدة هل يكون حكمه حكم اللقطة؟ قال : يحفظ حتى يظهر المالك. وفي التجريد لو رهن عبدين أو ثوبين ولم يسم لكل واحد شيئاً . من الدين يقسم الدين على قيمة تلك الأشياء، فما أصاب كل واحد وهو مضمون بأقل من قيمته ومما سمى أو رهن شاتين بثلاثين أحدهما بعشرة والأخرى بعشرين ولم يبين أيهما لم يجز لأن الجهالة تقع بينهما منازعة عند الهلاك فإنه إذا هلكت إحداهما لا يدري لا يسقط من الدين بأداء عشرة أو عشرين فيتنازعان في ذهاب الدين ،بهلاكها، فلو بين فهلك إحداهما سقط من الدين بقدرها لأنه لما بين حصة كل واحد منهما من الدين انقطعت المنازعة. وفي المنتقى : ولو قال رهنتك النخل بأصوله جاز إذا سمى بأصوله وإن لم يسم بأصوله لم يجز لأنه لا يقوم إلا بأصوله فلا يمكن تسليمه ،بدونه وذكر الفقيه أبو الليث روى أبو يوسف عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى في رجل رهن عند رجل جارية لها زوج فالرهن جائز لأن النكاح لا يوجب نقصاً في الرق والمالية وليس للمرتهن منع الزوج من غشيانها لأنه رهنها وهي مشغولة بحق الزوج وحق المرتهن لا يتعلق بمنافع البضع فحق الزوج فيها لا يفسد الرهن، فإن وطئها من ذلك سقط الدين لأن الوطء من الزوج ليس بجناية فأشبه الموت من المرض. قال أبو يوسف رحمه الله تعالى : ولو رهن جارية لا زوج لها فزوجها الراهن برضى المرتهن فهذا مثل الأول، ولو زوجها بغير رضا المرتهن جاز النكاح لقيام ملكه فيها وللمرتهن أن يمنعه من غشيانها لأن النكاح لم يعقد برضاه وثبوت حقه من الحبس سابق على تعلق حق الزوج غشيها فالمهر رهن معها، وإن لم يغشها لم يكن المهر رهناً معها لأن له أن يمنعه من الوطء فإن مات من غشيانها، فإن شاء المرتهن ضمن الراهن وإن شاء ضمن الزوج، فإن ضمن الزوج يرجع على المولى إن كتم الرهن عنه لأنه هو الذي أوقعه فيه، وإن لم يكن كتمه عنه لا يرجع . ابن سماعة عن أي يوسف رحمه الله : رجل أعتق ما في بطن جاريته ثم رهنها المولى فالرهن جائز لأنها مملوكة لمولاه، وإن ولدت فنقصتها الولادة لم يذهب من الدين شيء بنقصان الولادة لأنه إذا رهنها وهي حامل والحمل لا له من الولادة والولادة لا تنفك عن النقصان عادة فهذا النقصان حصل بسبب في يد الراهن فلا يكون مضموناً على المرتهن، ولو كان عليه دينار فدفع إليه دينارين فقال خذ أحدهما قضاء يكون لك فضاعا قبل أن أخذ فدينه
Book of Pledge: Chapter on what is permissible to take as pledge and what to pledge with and what is not permissible. Because of this, it is guaranteed. And likewise al-Halwani mentioned in his commentary. And al-Khujandi was asked about a man who pledged with another and his wife became surety for the debt owner with the husband's permission, then the debt owner demanded the surety to pay off the debt, so the judge imprisoned him and he was unable to pay; does the judge have the right to sell the pledge? He said: according to the Imam's statement, no; according to them both, yes. And Abu al-Fadl was asked about a man who pledged a house with another for one year for a debt on the pledger and the mortgagee took possession of the house; does the term invalidate the pledge? He said: if the term was in the pledge, it is invalid; if it was in the debt, it is not invalid. Likewise in al-Idah, he was asked about the mortgagee if he dies and his heirs know of the pledge but do not know the pledger and they seek to be free of responsibility; is its ruling the ruling of a lost item? He said: it is kept until the owner appears. Commentary

Key Terms
حق الحبس (haqq al-habs): The mortgagee's right to detain the pledged property until the debt is paid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pledger marries his pledged slave-girl without the mortgagee's consent, what is the mortgagee's right regarding the husband's intercourse?
A) He cannot prevent it.
B) He can prevent it.
C) He can dissolve the marriage.
D) He can demand the dowry.

Key Takeaway
Marriage of a pledged slave-girl after the pledge without the mortgagee's consent gives the mortgagee the right to prevent intercourse, and liability for death may fall on both pledger and husband.

Pregnant Slave-girl Pledged – Diminishment from Birth Not Compensable
Fatwa on pledging a pregnant slave-girl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that pledging a pregnant slave-girl is valid, and any diminishment in her value due to childbirth is not compensable by the mortgagee.

Core Idea
Natural childbirth is an expected event; the resulting loss in value is on the pledger, not the mortgagee.

This passage from Ibn Sama'ah from Abu Yusuf addresses the pledge of a pregnant slave-girl. The ruling is that the pledge is valid because the slave-girl remains owned by the pledger. When she gives birth, her value decreases due to the normal effects of childbirth. This natural diminishment does not entitle the mortgagee to compensation because it occurred through a cause in the pledger's hand (the pregnancy), not due to the mortgagee's fault.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
A man emancipates the fetus (what is in the belly) then pledges the slave-girl. The fetus is not part of the pledge.
The text says 'أعتق ما في بطن جاريته ثم رهنها المولى'.
2
Validity of pledge
The pledge is valid because she is still owned by the master (the pledger).
The text says 'فالرهن جائز لأنها مملوكة لمولاه'.
3
Effect of childbirth
When she gives birth, her value decreases (a natural effect). This diminishment does not reduce the debt or require compensation from the mortgagee.
The text says 'فإن ولدت فنقصتها الولادة لم يذهب من الدين شيء بنقصان الولادة'.
4
Reason
The pregnancy existed at the time of pledge, and childbirth is a normal consequence. The loss is attributed to the pledger's side.
The text says 'لأنه إذا رهنها وهي حامل والحمل لا له من الولادة والولادة لا تنفك عن النقصان عادة فهذا النقصان حصل بسبب في يد الراهن فلا يكون مضموناً على المرتهن'.

Source Text

If he specifies, and one perishes, that amount is discharged from the debt because when he specified the share of each from the debt, dispute is cut off. In al-Muntaqa: if he says 'I pledge the palm trees with their roots to you', it is valid if he specifies 'with their roots'; if he does not specify, it is not valid because they are only valuable with their roots, so delivery is not possible without them. And al-Faqih Abu al-Layth mentioned: Abu Yusuf reported from Abu Hanifa regarding a man who pledges a slave-girl who has a husband; the pledge is valid because marriage does not cause diminishment in slavery and value, and the mortgagee cannot prevent the husband from having intercourse with her because he pledged her while she is occupied with the husband's right, and the mortgagee's right does not attach to the usufruct of the vulva, so the husband's right does not invalidate the pledge. If he dies from that intercourse, the debt is discharged because the husband's intercourse is not a crime, so it resembles death from illness. Abu Yusuf said: if he pledges a slave-girl without a husband and the pledger marries her with the mortgagee's consent, this is like the first case. If he marries her without the mortgagee's consent, the marriage is valid due to his ownership, and the mortgagee can prevent him from intercourse because the marriage was not contracted with his consent and his right of detention preceded the husband's right. If he has intercourse with her, the dowry is pledged with her; if he does not have intercourse, the dowry is not pledged with her because he can prevent intercourse. If she dies from his intercourse, the mortgagee may either hold the pledger liable or hold the husband liable. If he holds the husband liable, the husband may recourse to the master if he concealed the pledge from him; if he did not conceal it, he cannot recourse. Ibn Sama'ah from Abu Yusuf: a man emancipated what was in the belly of his slave-girl, then the master pledged her; the pledge is valid because she is owned by her master. If she gives birth and the delivery diminishes her, nothing of the debt is lost due to the diminishment because when he pledged her while she was pregnant and delivery necessarily causes diminishment, this diminishment occurred by a cause in the pledger's hand, so it is not guaranteed upon the mortgagee. If he owed a dinar and gave him two dinars and said 'take one as payment and it is for you,' and they perished before he took, his debt is [unfinished].
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on various issues related to the validity and effects of pledges (rahn). It opens with a case involving a wife's suretyship: if she becomes a surety with her husband's permission and the judge imprisons her due to inability to pay, can the pledge be sold? Abu Hanifa says no, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say yes. Next, a term (ajal) in the pledge itself invalidates it, but a term in the debt does not. If the mortgagee dies and heirs know of the pledge but not the pledger, the pledge is treated like a lost item until the owner appears. When multiple items are pledged without specifying each's portion of the debt, the debt is divided proportionally to value; if one perishes, only its portion is discharged. If two sheep are pledged for thirty, one for ten and the other for twenty, specifying is necessary to avoid disputes. Pledging palm trees with roots is valid if specified; without specification it is invalid because roots are essential. A married slave-girl can be pledged because marriage does not reduce her value; the mortgagee cannot prevent the husband's intercourse. If the husband's intercourse causes her death, the debt is discharged. If the pledger marries a slave-girl after pledging her without the mortgagee's consent, the mortgagee can prevent intercourse. If she dies from intercourse, the mortgagee may choose whom to hold liable. A pregnant slave-girl can be pledged; if delivery diminishes her value, no compensation is required. The last case about two dinars is incomplete but shows the importance of specifying the purpose (payment vs pledge) when giving money.

Key Terms
الولادة (al-wiladah): Childbirth; the act of giving birth. Here, the natural process that may diminish the slave-girl's value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a pregnant slave-girl is pledged and she gives birth, reducing her value, what happens to the debt?
A) The debt is reduced by the amount of the loss.
B) The debt remains the same.
C) The mortgagee must pay compensation to the pledger.
D) The pledge becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
Natural diminishment of a pledged pregnant animal due to childbirth does not reduce the debt or require compensation.

Rahn — Pledge

Invalid Pledges: Amanat, Darak, and Mabi'
Commentary on why pledges are invalid with trusts, warranty, and sold items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three categories of invalid pledges in Hanafi fiqh and explain the key principles (amanat non-guarantee, darak contingency, mabi' owned) using the dalil of qiyas and istihsan.

Core Idea
A pledge requires the property to be guaranteed; trusts are not, darak is contingent, and sold items are already owned — all fail.

This lesson unpacks why certain categories of property cannot serve as pledges (rahn) in Hanafi law. The text from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delineate the conditions for a valid pledge: the pledged item must be guaranteed (madhmun) to allow extraction (istifa') of the debt. Trusts (amanat) are not guaranteed, darak (warranty of title) is only a contingent obligation, and a sold item (mabi') is already owned by the creditor. The commentary uses analogical reasoning (qiyas) and juristic preference (istihsan) to explain exceptions like the promised debt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and the three exceptions
Read the matn: 'Nor with trusts, nor with darak, nor with sold items. Rather it is valid only for a debt, even if promised, and for the capital of salam.' Understand that the pledge must be for a current or promised debt, but not for these three categories.
The rule is that the pledged item must be guaranteed. Trusts, darak, and sold items lack guarantee.
2
Analyze trusts (amanat): why they fail
The commentary explains that trusts like deposits, loans for use, mudarabah, and partnership property are not guaranteed (ghayr madhmun). Since a pledge is a form of extraction (istifa'), it requires the pledged item to be guaranteed. The analogy is made to a slave who committed a crime or a slave permitted to trade—these are not guaranteed and thus cannot be pledged.
Contrast with guaranteed properties like usurped goods, khul' compensation, dowry, etc., which can be pledged.
3
Analyze darak (warranty of title): contingency
Darak is a guarantee of the price if the sold property is claimed by a third party. It is not an immediate obligation; it only arises after the claim and judicial ruling. Since istifa' cannot precede obligation, darak cannot be pledged. The commentary distinguishes suretyship for darak, which is valid because kafalah can be conditional.
If a pledge is taken for darak before obligation, it is void and the property perishes as a trust.
4
Contrast with the promised debt: istihsan
Unlike darak, a pledge for a promised debt (e.g., 'I pledge this for you to lend me a thousand') is valid by istihsan. The promise is treated as existence due to need. If the pledge perishes before the loan, the mortgagee is liable for the lesser of the named amount or the value. If no amount is named, the mortgagee chooses what to pay.
Abu Yusuf differs: if no amount is named, the mortgagee guarantees the full value (like property taken for purchase).
5
Note the sold items (mabi') and the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Sold items are not valid because they are already owned by the buyer (creditor) and guaranteed by the price, not by themselves. The commentary also mentions a report from Abu Yusuf requiring full value for unnamed promised debt.
The mufta bihi is the lesser of named amount or value, but caution suggests following Abu Yusuf.

[Not valid] with trusts, nor with darak (warranty of title), nor with sold items. Rather it is valid only for a debt, even if promised, and for the capital of salam. It remains as it is, and he is trusted because there is no claim and taking except after possession, and possession of an unknown [thing] is inconceivable. And if he said 'I take both as payment for you,' it is possession for his debt, and this does not resemble this pledge. The guarantee. Intentional. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And not) with trusts, darak, and sold items, meaning the pledge is not valid with these things. As for trusts like deposit, loan for use, mudarabah, and partnership property, because the pledge is guaranteed by what it is pledged for due to being taking, so the pledge must be guaranteed to be a pledge and its taking from the pledge is realized. Trusts are not guaranteed, nor can they be taken from their essence while they remain, nor is obligation after their destruction, so it becomes like the slave who committed an offense, the slave permitted to trade, and preemption is not guaranteed upon the buyer. This differs from guaranteed properties like the usurped, the substitute of khul', the dowry, and the substitute of reconciliation for blood, where the pledge is valid with them because the obligation is determined; the obligated amount is the value, and the property is a substitute according to the majority, and for the value there is a semblance of obligation as some said, so it is a pledge with what is impossible due to its obligation and cause. As for darak, because the pledge is taking, and there is no taking before obligation, because the meaning of darak is guarantee of the price when the sold item is claimed; what is not claimed does not obligate the seller to return the price, and likewise after claim until a ruling is given to return the price and the sale is rescinded, due to the possibility that the claimant may ratify the sale. This differs from suretyship for it, where it is permissible because suretyship can be attached to a suitable condition, as known in its place, because it is an undertaking of demand, and undertaking of actions conditionally or added to property is permissible, as in fasting and prayer, and there is no element of ownership in it. Not so the pledge, for it is taking and thus ownership, and all ownerships cannot be made conditional or added, so they differ. And if the pledge is taken for darak before the obligation of claim, and it perishes in the buyer's hand, it perishes as a trust because there is no contract at that time, so it is invalid. This differs from the pledge for a promised debt, like saying 'I pledge this to you for a thousand, to lend me,' and it perishes in the mortgagee's hand: it perishes for what is named of the money, because the promised is treated as existing due to need; rather it is made existing for the purpose of taking, because the pledge is taking and taking does not precede obligation but follows it, and existence must precede for the taking to be based on it. And because it is taken by way of a pledge that is valid based on its existence, so it is given its ruling like property taken for purpose of purchase, so it is guaranteed by the lesser of what is named and the value of the pledge if he named the amount of the promised. If he did not name its amount, such as pledging for him to give him something, and the pledge perishes in his hand, the mortgagee gives the pledger what he wishes because by perishing he is considered to have taken something, so its clarification is up to him as if he admitted it. And from Abu Yusuf: if he said 'Lend me and take this as pledge' and did not name anything, and it perishes, he guarantees the value of the pledge, unlike property taken for purpose of purchase where the taker must pay its full value because it is guaranteed by itself like a corrupt sale or usurped property, so it is not quantified by something else. Not so the pledge, for it is guaranteed by something else, namely the debt, so it is quantified by it. And al-Mu'alla reported from Abu Yusuf that the value of the pledge is owed in the promised debt no matter how much, like property taken for the purpose of purchase. As for sold items, because it is guaranteed by something else, the price. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq vol. 29.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining why a pledge (rahn) is not valid with three categories: trusts (amanat), warranty of title (darak), and sold items (mabi'). The commentator first states the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq: 'Nor with trusts, nor with darak, nor with sold items. Rather it is valid only for a debt, even if promised, and for the capital of salam.' The commentary then unpacks each category. Trusts: deposits, loans for use, mudarabah, and partnership property are not guaranteed; since a pledge must be guaranteed (because it serves as extraction of debt), trusts fail. This is analogized to a slave who committed a crime or a slave permitted to trade—these are not guaranteed. However, guaranteed properties like usurped goods, khul' compensation, dowry, and blood money settlement are valid pledges because they obligate value. Darak (warranty of title): the pledge is a form of extraction (istifa'), which cannot precede obligation. Darak is a guarantee of the price only if the property is claimed; it is contingent, not yet obligatory. Suretyship (kafalah) for darak is allowed because kafalah can be conditional and does not involve ownership transfer, unlike rahn which is like ownership. If a pledge is taken for darak before obligation, it is void and the property perishes as a trust. This is contrasted with a pledge for a promised debt: if someone says 'I pledge this for you to lend me a thousand,' and the pledge perishes before the loan is given, it is still valid and the mortgagee is liable for the lesser of the named amount or the value, because the promise is treated as existing due to need. If no amount is named, the mortgagee must pay what he wishes. Abu Yusuf differs: if no amount is named, he guarantees the full value. There is also a report that Abu Yusuf requires the full value always, like property taken for purpose of purchase. Finally, sold items (mabi') are not valid as pledges because they are already owned by the creditor (the buyer) and are guaranteed by the price, not by themselves.

Key Terms
الأمانات (al-amanat): Properties held in trust: deposits, loans for use, mudarabah capital, partnership assets – not guaranteed against loss.
الدرك (al-darak): Warranty of title; the seller's obligation to refund the price if the sold property is legally claimed by a third party.
الاستيفاء (al-istifa'): Extraction or taking of something due, such as a debt. The pledge is considered a means of extracting the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because a deposit is not a debt.

C) Because the pledge must be on a guaranteed thing, but deposits are not guaranteed.
D) Because the deposit cannot be possessed.

Key Takeaway
A pledge (rahn) in Hanafi fiqh requires the pledged property to be guaranteed; trusts, contingent obligations, and already-owned items fail this condition, though a promised debt is allowed by istihsan.

Ruling on Invalid Pledges: Trusts, Damages, and Sold Item
Explains why amanat, darak, and mabi' cannot be used as pledges.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why pledges with trusts, darak, and the sold item are invalid in Hanafi fiqh and apply the distinction between rahn and kafalah.

Core Idea
A pledge requires a guaranteed obligation; trusts and contingent claims are not guaranteed, so invalid.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the Hanafi ruling that three types of items cannot be used as pledges: trusts (amanat), damages (darak), and the sold item (mabi'). The reasoning hinges on the requirement that a pledged item must be guaranteed (mamun bihi) and the obligation present at the time of contract. Understanding these exceptions sharpens your grasp of the essential conditions of rahn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three invalid pledges
List the three categories the author prohibits: trusts (amanat), damages (darak), and the sold item (mabi').
The sold item likely refers to the item being sold before transfer of ownership; the obligation is not yet present.
2
Understand the core requirement: guaranteed item
A pledge is a form of collection (istifa'), so the item must be guaranteed (mamun bihi) to fulfill that purpose.
The text states: 'الرهن مضمون بما رهن به' – the pledge is guaranteed by what it is taken for.
3
Analyze why trusts are invalid
Trusts (e.g., deposit, loan for use, partnership capital) are not guaranteed – if lost, no liability. Thus they cannot secure a debt.
Analogies given: slave who commits crime, preemption right – all non-guaranteed.
4
Analyze why darak is invalid
Darak is a guarantee of price upon revocation of sale; it is contingent on future occurrence. No collection before obligation exists.
Even after revocation, it is conditional on the rightful owner not validating the sale.
5
Distinguish rahn from kafalah
Kafalah (personal guarantee) can be conditional because it is a mere undertaking (iltizam al-mutalaba), while rahn involves ownership transfer (tamlik) and cannot be conditional or future-based.
This contrast explains why kafalah is permissible with conditions but rahn is not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرهن باب ما يجوز ارتهانه والارتهان به وما لا يجوز
قال رحمه الله: (ولا) بالأمانات وبالدرك وبالمبيع أي لا يجوز الرهن بهذه الأشياء أما بالأمانات كالوديعة والعارية والمضاربة ومال الشركة فلأن الرهن مضمون بما رهن به لكونه استيفاء فلا بد من ضمان المرهون به ليقع الرهن مضموناً ويتحقق استيفاؤه من الرهن، والأمانات ليست بمضمونة ولا يمكن استيفاؤها من عينها حال بقائها وعدم وجوب بعد هلاكها فصار كالعبد الجاني والعبد المأذون له في التجارة والشفعة غير مضمونة على المشتري بخلاف الأعيان المضمونة كالمغصوب وبدل الخلع والمهر وبدل الصلح عن دم حيث يصح الرهن بها لأن الوجوب فيها يتقدر إذا الواجب فيها القيمة والعين مخلص على ما عليه الجمهور وللقيمة فيها شبهة الوجوب على ما قاله البعض فيكون رهناً بما تعذر وجوبه وسببه . وأما الدرك فلأن الرهن استيفاء ولا استيفاء قبل الوجوب لأن معنى الدرك ضمان الثمن عند استحقاق المبيع فما لا يستحق لا يجب على البائع رد الثمن وكذا بعد الاستحقاق حتى يحكم برد الثمن ويفسخ البيع لاحتمال أن يجيز المستحق البيع بخلاف الكفالة به حيث تجوز لأن الكفالة يجوز تعلقها بشرط ملائم على ما عرف في موضعه لأنها التزام المطالبة والتزام الأفعال معلقاً أو مضافاً إلى المال جائز كما في الصوم والصلاة وليس فيها شيء من معنى التمليك ولا كذلك الرهن فإنه استيفاء فيكون تمليكاً، والتمليكات بأسرها لا يجوز تعليقها ولا إضافتها فافترقا .
Book of Pledge: Chapter: What is valid to take as a pledge and to pledge by, and what is not valid. He (the author) said: "And not by trusts, nor by damages, nor by the sold item." That is, it is not permissible to pledge with these things. As for trusts like deposits, loans for use, partnerships, and partnership property, because the pledge is guaranteed by what it is pledged for because it is a collection (istifa'), so there must be a guarantee of the thing pledged for so that the pledge becomes guaranteed and its collection from the pledge is realized, and trusts are not guaranteed and cannot be collected from their actual substance while they exist and there is no obligation after their destruction, so it becomes like the slave who commits a crime, the slave permitted to trade, and preemption (shuf'a) which is not guaranteed for the buyer, contrary to guaranteed items like the usurped item, the consideration for khul', the mahr, and the consideration for settlement for blood, where the pledge is valid because the obligation is measured—since the obligation here is the value and the actual substance is a substitute according to the majority, and there is a semblance of obligation for the value according to some—so it becomes a pledge for what is not obligatory or its cause is not obligatory. As for damages (darak), because the pledge is collection, and there is no collection before obligation, because the meaning of darak is guarantee of the price when the sold item is revoked; so if it is not revoked, the seller is not obliged to return the price, and even after revocation until a judgment is made to return the price and the sale is rescinded due to the possibility that the rightful owner may validate the sale, unlike a guarantee (kafala) which is permissible because guarantee can be attached with a suitable condition as known in its place, because it is an undertaking of claim and undertaking of acts conditionally or added to property is permissible as in fasting and prayer, and it does not contain any meaning of ownership, unlike the pledge because it is collection and so is ownership, and all ownership transactions cannot be conditional or added, so they differ.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (Hidayah-style) explaining the types of items that cannot be used as a pledge (rahn) in Hanafi fiqh. The author states that three categories are invalid: trusts (amanat), damages (darak), and the sold item (mabi'). The commentary provides the legal reasoning for each. For trusts (like deposit, loan for use, partnership capital), the key point is that a pledge must be guaranteed (mamun bihi) because it is a form of collection (istifa'). Trusts are not guaranteed; if they are destroyed, there is no liability, so they cannot secure a debt. The text analogizes this to slaves who commit crimes or are permitted to trade, and preemption rights. In contrast, guaranteed items like usurped goods, mahr, and khul' consideration are valid because they involve a known obligation. For damages (darak, the guarantee of the price in case of revocation), the reason is that the obligation to return the price does not exist at the time of the pledge, and it may never arise if the rightful owner validates the sale. The text contrasts this with a personal guarantee (kafalah), which can be conditional because it is a mere undertaking of claim, not a transfer of ownership. Pledge, being a form of ownership transfer (tamlik), cannot be conditional or future-based. This distinction (tafriq) between rahn and kafalah is critical.

Key Terms
أمانات (amanat): Items held in trust without liability for loss, such as deposits, loans for use, and partnership capital.
الدرك (al-darak): Guarantee of the price of a sold item if it is revoked due to a defect in title.
الكفالة (al-kafalah): Personal guarantee or surety, which is permissible conditionally because it is a claim undertaking, not ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it invalid to pledge a deposit (wadi'ah) according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the deposit is not owned by the pledgor.
B) Because a deposit is a trust and not guaranteed; thus it cannot secure a debt.
C) Because the deposit is a form of riba.
D) Because the deposit is already a pledge itself.

Key Takeaway
A valid pledge requires the item to be a guaranteed, present obligation; trusts and contingent obligations fail this and invalidate the contract.
